  1652	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tVII.
  1653	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1654	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tHROTHGAR AND BEOWULF.
  1655	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1656	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1657	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar remembers Beowulf as a youth, and also remembers his father.}
  1658	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1659	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hrothgar answered, helm of the Scyldings:
  1660	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "I remember this man as the merest of striplings.
  1661	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His father long dead now was Ecgtheow titled,
  1662	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Him Hrethel the Geatman granted at home his
  1663	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 One only daughter; his battle-brave son
  1664	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Is come but now, sought a trustworthy friend.
  1665	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Seafaring sailors asserted it then,
  1666	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1667	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is reported to have the strength of thirty men.}
  1668	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1669	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who valuable gift-gems of the Geatmen[1] carried
  1670	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As peace-offering thither, that he thirty men's grapple
  1671	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Has in his hand, the hero-in-battle.
  1672	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1673	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{God hath sent him to our rescue.}
  1674	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1675	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The holy Creator usward sent him,
  1676	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To West-Dane warriors, I ween, for to render
  1677	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Gainst Grendel's grimness gracious assistance:
  1678	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I shall give to the good one gift-gems for courage.
  1679	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Hasten to bid them hither to speed them,[2]
  1680	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To see assembled this circle of kinsmen;
  1681	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Tell them expressly they're welcome in sooth to
  1682	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The men of the Danes." To the door of the building
  1683	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1684	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[15]
  1685	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1686	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wulfgar invites the strangers in.}
  1687	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1688	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wulfgar went then, this word-message shouted:
  1689	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 "My victorious liegelord bade me to tell you,
  1690	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The East-Danes' atheling, that your origin knows he,
  1691	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And o'er wave-billows wafted ye welcome are hither,
  1692	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Valiant of spirit. Ye straightway may enter
  1693	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Clad in corslets, cased in your helmets,
  1694	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 To see King Hrothgar. Here let your battle-boards,
  1695	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wood-spears and war-shafts, await your conferring."
  1696	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The mighty one rose then, with many a liegeman,
  1697	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          An excellent thane-group; some there did await them,
  1698	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And as bid of the brave one the battle-gear guarded.
  1699	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Together they hied them, while the hero did guide them,
  1700	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath Heorot's roof; the high-minded went then
  1701	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sturdy 'neath helmet till he stood in the building.
  1702	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf spake (his burnie did glisten,
  1703	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His armor seamed over by the art of the craftsman):
  1704	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1705	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf salutes Hrothgar, and then proceeds to boast of his youthful
  1706	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tachievements.}
  1707	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1708	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 "Hail thou, Hrothgar! I am Higelac's kinsman
  1709	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And vassal forsooth; many a wonder
  1710	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I dared as a stripling. The doings of Grendel,
  1711	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In far-off fatherland I fully did know of:
  1712	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sea-farers tell us, this hall-building standeth,
  1713	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Excellent edifice, empty and useless
  1714	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To all the earlmen after evenlight's glimmer
  1715	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath heaven's bright hues hath hidden its glory.
  1716	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          This my earls then urged me, the most excellent of them,
  1717	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Carles very clever, to come and assist thee,
  1718	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Folk-leader Hrothgar; fully they knew of
  1719	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1720	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{His fight with the nickers.}
  1721	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1722	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The strength of my body. Themselves they beheld me
  1723	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When I came from the contest, when covered with gore
  1724	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Foes I escaped from, where five[3] I had bound,
  1725	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[16]      The giant-race wasted, in the waters destroying
  1726	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 The nickers by night, bore numberless sorrows,
  1727	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Weders avenged (woes had they suffered)
  1728	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Enemies ravaged; alone now with Grendel
  1729	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1730	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He intends to fight Grendel unaided.}
  1731	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1732	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I shall manage the matter, with the monster of evil,
  1733	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The giant, decide it. Thee I would therefore
  1734	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Beg of thy bounty, Bright-Danish chieftain,
  1735	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lord of the Scyldings, this single petition:
  1736	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not to refuse me, defender of warriors,
  1737	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Friend-lord of folks, so far have I sought thee,
  1738	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That _I_ may unaided, my earlmen assisting me,
  1739	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 This brave-mooded war-band, purify Heorot.
  1740	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I have heard on inquiry, the horrible creature
  1741	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1742	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Since the monster uses no weapons,}
  1743	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1744	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From veriest rashness recks not for weapons;
  1745	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I this do scorn then, so be Higelac gracious,
  1746	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My liegelord belovèd, lenient of spirit,
  1747	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 To bear a blade or a broad-fashioned target,
  1748	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A shield to the onset; only with hand-grip
  1749	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1750	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I, too, shall disdain to use any.}
  1751	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1752	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The foe I must grapple, fight for my life then,
  1753	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Foeman with foeman; he fain must rely on
  1754	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The doom of the Lord whom death layeth hold of.
  1755	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1756	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Should he crush me, he will eat my companions as he has eaten thy
  1757	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tthanes.}
  1758	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1759	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 I ween he will wish, if he win in the struggle,
  1760	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To eat in the war-hall earls of the Geat-folk,
  1761	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Boldly to swallow[4] them, as of yore he did often
  1762	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The best of the Hrethmen! Thou needest not trouble
  1763	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A head-watch to give me;[5] he will have me dripping
  1764	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1765	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[17]
  1766	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1767	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{In case of my defeat, thou wilt not have the trouble of burying me.}
  1768	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1769	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 And dreary with gore, if death overtake me,[6]
  1770	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Will bear me off bleeding, biting and mouthing me,
  1771	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hermit will eat me, heedless of pity,
  1772	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Marking the moor-fens; no more wilt thou need then
  1773	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1774	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Should I fall, send my armor to my lord, King Higelac.}
  1775	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1776	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Find me my food.[7] If I fall in the battle,
  1777	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 Send to Higelac the armor that serveth
  1778	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To shield my bosom, the best of equipments,
  1779	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Richest of ring-mails; 'tis the relic of Hrethla,
  1780	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1781	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Weird is supreme}
  1782	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1783	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The work of Wayland. Goes Weird as she must go!"
  1784	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1785	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] Some render 'gif-sceattas' by 'tribute.'--'Géata' B. and Th.
  1786	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    emended to 'Géatum.' If this be accepted, change '_of_ the Geatmen' to
  1787	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    '_to_ the Geatmen.'
  1788	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1789	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] If t.B.'s emendation of vv. 386, 387 be accepted, the two lines,
  1790	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'Hasten ... kinsmen' will read: _Hasten thou, bid the throng of
  1791	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    kinsmen go into the hall together_.
  1792	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1793	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] For 420 (_b_) and 421 (_a_), B. suggests: Þær ic (on) fífelgeban
  1794	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    ýðde eotena cyn = _where I in the ocean destroyed the
  1795	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    eoten-race_.--t.B. accepts B.'s "brilliant" 'fífelgeban,' omits 'on,'
  1796	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    emends 'cyn' to 'hám,' arranging: Þær ic fífelgeban ýðde, eotena hám =
  1797	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    _where I desolated the ocean, the home of the eotens_.--This would be
  1798	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    better but for changing 'cyn' to 'hám.'--I suggest: Þær ic fífelgeband
  1799	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (cf. nhd. Bande) ýðde, eotena cyn = _where I conquered the monster
  1800	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    band, the race of the eotens_. This makes no change except to read
  1801	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    '_fífel_' for '_fífe_.'
  1802	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1803	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [4] 'Unforhte' (444) is much disputed.--H.-So. wavers between adj. and
  1804	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    adv. Gr. and B. take it as an adv. modifying _etan: Will eat the Geats
  1805	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    fearlessly_.--Kl. considers this reading absurd, and proposes
  1806	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'anforhte' = timid.--Understanding 'unforhte' as an adj. has this
  1807	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    advantage, viz. that it gives a parallel to 'Geátena leóde': but to
  1808	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    take it as an adv. is more natural. Furthermore, to call the Geats
  1809	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'brave' might, at this point, seem like an implied thrust at the
  1810	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Danes, so long helpless; while to call his own men 'timid' would be
  1811	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    befouling his own nest.
  1812	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1813	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [5] For 'head-watch,' cf. H.-So. notes and cf. v. 2910.--Th.
  1814	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    translates: _Thou wilt not need my head to hide_ (i.e., thou wilt have
  1815	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    no occasion to bury me, as Grendel will devour me whole).--Simrock
  1816	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    imagines a kind of dead-watch.--Dr. H. Wood suggests: _Thou wilt not
  1817	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    have to bury so much as my head_ (for Grendel will be a thorough
  1818	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    undertaker),--grim humor.
  1819	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1820	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [6] S. proposes a colon after 'nimeð' (l. 447). This would make no
  1821	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    essential change in the translation.
  1822	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1823	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [7] Owing to the vagueness of 'feorme' (451), this passage is
  1824	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    variously translated. In our translation, H.-So.'s glossary has been
  1825	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    quite closely followed. This agrees substantially with B.'s
  1826	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    translation (P. and B. XII. 87). R. translates: _Thou needst not take
  1827	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    care longer as to the consumption of my dead body._ 'Líc' is also a
  1828	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    crux here, as it may mean living body or dead body.

  1838	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar responds.}
  1839	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1840	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hrothgar discoursed, helm of the Scyldings:
  1841	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "To defend our folk and to furnish assistance,[1]
  1842	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thou soughtest us hither, good friend Beowulf.
  1843	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1844	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Reminiscences of Beowulf's father, Ecgtheow.}
  1845	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1846	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The fiercest of feuds thy father engaged in,
  1847	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Heatholaf killed he in hand-to-hand conflict
  1848	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Mid Wilfingish warriors; then the Wederish people
  1849	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For fear of a feud were forced to disown him.
  1850	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thence flying he fled to the folk of the South-Danes,
  1851	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[18]      The race of the Scyldings, o'er the roll of the waters;
  1852	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 I had lately begun then to govern the Danemen,
  1853	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hoard-seat of heroes held in my youth,
  1854	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Rich in its jewels: dead was Heregar,
  1855	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My kinsman and elder had earth-joys forsaken,
  1856	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Healfdene his bairn. He was better than I am!
  1857	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 That feud thereafter for a fee I compounded;
  1858	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          O'er the weltering waters to the Wilfings I sent
  1859	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ornaments old; oaths did he swear me.
  1860	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1861	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar recounts to Beowulf the horrors of Grendel's persecutions.}
  1862	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1863	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          It pains me in spirit to any to tell it,
  1864	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          What grief in Heorot Grendel hath caused me,
  1865	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 What horror unlooked-for, by hatred unceasing.
  1866	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Waned is my war-band, wasted my hall-troop;
  1867	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Weird hath offcast them to the clutches of Grendel.
  1868	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          God can easily hinder the scather
  1869	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From deeds so direful. Oft drunken with beer
  1870	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1871	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{My thanes have made many boasts, but have not executed them.}
  1872	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1873	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 O'er the ale-vessel promised warriors in armor
  1874	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They would willingly wait on the wassailing-benches
  1875	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A grapple with Grendel, with grimmest of edges.
  1876	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then this mead-hall at morning with murder was reeking,
  1877	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The building was bloody at breaking of daylight,
  1878	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 The bench-deals all flooded, dripping and bloodied,
  1879	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The folk-hall was gory: I had fewer retainers,
  1880	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Dear-beloved warriors, whom death had laid hold of.
  1881	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1882	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Sit down to the feast, and give us comfort.}
  1883	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1884	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sit at the feast now, thy intents unto heroes,[2]
  1885	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thy victor-fame show, as thy spirit doth urge thee!"
  1886	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1887	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A bench is made ready for Beowulf and his party.}
  1888	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1889	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 For the men of the Geats then together assembled,
  1890	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the beer-hall blithesome a bench was made ready;
  1891	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          There warlike in spirit they went to be seated,
  1892	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Proud and exultant. A liegeman did service,
  1893	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[19]      Who a beaker embellished bore with decorum,
  1894	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1895	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The gleeman sings}
  1896	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1897	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 And gleaming-drink poured. The gleeman sang whilom
  1898	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1899	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The heroes all rejoice together.}
  1900	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1901	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hearty in Heorot; there was heroes' rejoicing,
  1902	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A numerous war-band of Weders and Danemen.
  1903	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1904	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] B. and S. reject the reading given in H.-So., and suggested by
  1905	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Grtvg. B. suggests for 457-458:
  1906	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1907	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t               wáere-ryhtum Þú, wine mín Béowulf,
  1908	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t               and for ár-stafum úsic sóhtest.
  1909	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1910	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    This means: _From the obligations of clientage, my friend Beowulf, and
  1911	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    for assistance thou hast sought us_.--This gives coherence to
  1912	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Hrothgar's opening remarks in VIII., and also introduces a new motive
  1913	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    for Beowulf's coming to Hrothgar's aid.
  1914	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1915	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] _Sit now at the feast, and disclose thy purposes to the victorious
  1916	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    heroes, as thy spirit urges_.--Kl. reaches the above translation by
  1917	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    erasing the comma after 'meoto' and reading 'sige-hrèðsecgum.'--There
  1918	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    are other and bolder emendations and suggestions. Of these the boldest
  1919	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    is to regard 'meoto' as a verb (imperative), and read 'on sæl': _Think
  1920	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    upon gayety, etc_.--All the renderings are unsatisfactory, the one
  1921	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    given in our translation involving a zeugma.

  1927	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1928	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tUNFERTH TAUNTS BEOWULF.
  1929	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1930	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1931	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Unferth, a thane of Hrothgar, is jealous of Beowulf, and undertakes to
  1932	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\ttwit him.}
  1933	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1934	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Unferth spoke up, Ecglaf his son,
  1935	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who sat at the feet of the lord of the Scyldings,
  1936	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Opened the jousting (the journey[1] of Beowulf,
  1937	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sea-farer doughty, gave sorrow to Unferth
  1938	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 And greatest chagrin, too, for granted he never
  1939	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That any man else on earth should attain to,
  1940	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gain under heaven, more glory than he):
  1941	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1942	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Did you take part in a swimming-match with Breca?}
  1943	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1944	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Art thou that Beowulf with Breca did struggle,
  1945	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On the wide sea-currents at swimming contended,
  1946	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Where to humor your pride the ocean ye tried,
  1947	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1948	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{'Twas mere folly that actuated you both to risk your lives on the ocean.}
  1949	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1950	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From vainest vaunting adventured your bodies
  1951	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In care of the waters? And no one was able
  1952	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nor lief nor loth one, in the least to dissuade you
  1953	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Your difficult voyage; then ye ventured a-swimming,
  1954	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Where your arms outstretching the streams ye did cover,
  1955	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The mere-ways measured, mixing and stirring them,
  1956	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Glided the ocean; angry the waves were,
  1957	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With the weltering of winter. In the water's possession,
  1958	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ye toiled for a seven-night; he at swimming outdid thee,
  1959	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 In strength excelled thee. Then early at morning
  1960	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On the Heathoremes' shore the holm-currents tossed him,
  1961	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sought he thenceward the home of his fathers,
  1962	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beloved of his liegemen, the land of the Brondings,
  1963	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The peace-castle pleasant, where a people he wielded,
  1964	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[20]   25 Had borough and jewels. The pledge that he made thee
  1965	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1966	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Breca outdid you entirely.}
  1967	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1968	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The son of Beanstan hath soothly accomplished.
  1969	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then I ween thou wilt find thee less fortunate issue,
  1970	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1971	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Much more will Grendel outdo you, if you vie with him in prowess.}
  1972	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1973	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though ever triumphant in onset of battle,
  1974	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A grim grappling, if Grendel thou darest
  1975	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 For the space of a night near-by to wait for!"
  1976	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1977	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf retaliates.}
  1978	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1979	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf answered, offspring of Ecgtheow:
  1980	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "My good friend Unferth, sure freely and wildly,
  1981	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1982	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{O friend Unferth, you are fuddled with beer, and cannot talk coherently.}
  1983	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1984	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thou fuddled with beer of Breca hast spoken,
  1985	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hast told of his journey! A fact I allege it,
  1986	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 That greater strength in the waters I had then,
  1987	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ills in the ocean, than any man else had.
  1988	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          We made agreement as the merest of striplings
  1989	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Promised each other (both of us then were
  1990	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1991	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{We simply kept an engagement made in early life.}
  1992	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1993	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Younkers in years) that we yet would adventure
  1994	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Out on the ocean; it all we accomplished.
  1995	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          While swimming the sea-floods, sword-blade unscabbarded
  1996	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Boldly we brandished, our bodies expected
  1997	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To shield from the sharks. He sure was unable
  1998	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  1999	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He _could_ not excel me, and I _would_ not excel him.}
  2000	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2001	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To swim on the waters further than I could,
  2002	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 More swift on the waves, nor _would_ I from him go.
  2003	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then we two companions stayed in the ocean
  2004	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2005	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{After five days the currents separated us.}
  2006	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2007	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Five nights together, till the currents did part us,
  2008	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The weltering waters, weathers the bleakest,
  2009	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And nethermost night, and the north-wind whistled
  2010	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Fierce in our faces; fell were the billows.
  2011	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The mere fishes' mood was mightily ruffled:
  2012	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And there against foemen my firm-knotted corslet,
  2013	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hand-jointed, hardy, help did afford me;
  2014	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My battle-sark braided, brilliantly gilded,
  2015	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2016	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A horrible sea-beast attacked me, but I slew him.}
  2017	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2018	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Lay on my bosom. To the bottom then dragged me,
  2019	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A hateful fiend-scather, seized me and held me,
  2020	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Grim in his grapple: 'twas granted me, nathless,
  2021	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To pierce the monster with the point of my weapon,
  2022	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My obedient blade; battle offcarried
  2023	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 The mighty mere-creature by means of my hand-blow.
  2024	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2025	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] It has been plausibly suggested that 'síð' (in 501 and in 353)
  2026	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    means 'arrival.' If so, translate the bracket: _(the arrival of
  2027	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Beowulf, the brave seafarer, was a source of great chagrin to Unferth,
  2028	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    etc.)_.

  2036	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2037	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF SILENCES UNFERTH.--GLEE IS HIGH.
  2038	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2039	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2040	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "So ill-meaning enemies often did cause me
  2041	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sorrow the sorest. I served them, in quittance,
  2042	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2043	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{My dear sword always served me faithfully.}
  2044	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2045	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With my dear-lovèd sword, as in sooth it was fitting;
  2046	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They missed the pleasure of feasting abundantly,
  2047	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Ill-doers evil, of eating my body,
  2048	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of surrounding the banquet deep in the ocean;
  2049	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But wounded with edges early at morning
  2050	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They were stretched a-high on the strand of the ocean,
  2051	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  2055	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 No longer thereafter were hindered from sailing
  2056	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The foam-dashing currents. Came a light from the east,

  2061	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2062	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The blustering crags. Weird often saveth
  2063	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 The undoomed hero if doughty his valor!

  2098	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2099	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thy mood as ferocious as thou dost describe them.
  2100	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He hath found out fully that the fierce-burning hatred,
  2101	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The edge-battle eager, of all of your kindred,

  2320	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the division usually made at this point, 'Þá.' (711), usually rendered
  2321	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'then,' he translates 'when,' and connects its clause with the
  2322	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    foregoing sentence. These changes he makes to reduce the number of
  2323	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'cóm's' as principal verbs. (Cf. 703, 711, 721.) With all deference to
  2324	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    this acute scholar, I must say that it seems to me that the poet is
  2325	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    exhausting his resources to bring out clearly the supreme event on
  2326	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    which the whole subsequent action turns. First, he (Grendel) came _in
  2327	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the wan night_; second, he came _from the moor_; third, he came _to
  2328	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the hall_. Time, place from which, place to which, are all given.

  2633	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A numerous host of the race of the scathers
  2634	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They had slain with the sword-edge. To Sigmund accrued then
  2635	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          No little of glory, when his life-days were over,
  2636	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since he sturdy in struggle had destroyed the great dragon,
  2637	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 The hoard-treasure's keeper; 'neath the hoar-grayish stone he,
  2638	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The son of the atheling, unaided adventured
  2639	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The perilous project; not present was Fitela,
  2640	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Yet the fortune befell him of forcing his weapon
  2641	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Through the marvellous dragon, that it stood in the wall,
  2642	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Well-honored weapon; the worm was slaughtered.
  2643	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The great one had gained then by his glorious achievement
  2644	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To reap from the ring-hoard richest enjoyment,
  2645	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[32]      As best it did please him: his vessel he loaded,
  2646	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Shining ornaments on the ship's bosom carried,
  2647	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Kinsman of Wæls: the drake in heat melted.
  2648	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2649	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Sigemund was widely famed.}
  2650	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2651	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He was farthest famed of fugitive pilgrims,
  2652	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mid wide-scattered world-folk, for works of great prowess,
  2653	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          War-troopers' shelter: hence waxed he in honor.[4]
  2654	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2655	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Heremod, an unfortunate Danish king, is introduced by way of contrast.}
  2656	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2657	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Afterward Heremod's hero-strength failed him,
  2658	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 His vigor and valor. 'Mid venomous haters
  2659	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the hands of foemen he was foully delivered,
  2660	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Offdriven early. Agony-billows
  2661	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2662	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Unlike Sigemund and Beowulf, Heremod was a burden to his people.}
  2663	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2664	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Oppressed him too long, to his people he became then,
  2665	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To all the athelings, an ever-great burden;
  2666	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 And the daring one's journey in days of yore
  2667	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Many wise men were wont to deplore,
  2668	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Such as hoped he would bring them help in their sorrow,
  2669	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That the son of their ruler should rise into power,
  2670	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Holding the headship held by his fathers,
  2671	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 Should govern the people, the gold-hoard and borough,
  2672	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The kingdom of heroes, the realm of the Scyldings.
  2673	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2674	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is an honor to his race.}
  2675	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2676	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He to all men became then far more beloved,
  2677	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Higelac's kinsman, to kindreds and races,
  2678	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To his friends much dearer; him malice assaulted.--
  2679	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2680	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The story is resumed.}
  2681	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  2683	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The dun-colored highways. Then the light of the morning

  2685	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the beautiful building, bold ones in spirit,

  2687	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       85 From his wife-bower wending, warden of treasures,
  2688	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Glorious trod with troopers unnumbered,
  2689	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Famed for his virtues, and with him the queen-wife
  2690	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Measured the mead-ways, with maidens attending.

  2719	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tHROTHGAR'S GRATITUDE.
  2720	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2721	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2722	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hrothgar discoursed (to the hall-building went he,
  2723	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He stood by the pillar,[1] saw the steep-rising hall-roof
  2724	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gleaming with gold-gems, and Grendel his hand there):
  2725	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2726	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar gives thanks for the overthrow of the monster.}
  2727	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2728	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "For the sight we behold now, thanks to the Wielder
  2729	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Early be offered! Much evil I bided,
  2730	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Snaring from Grendel:[2] God can e'er 'complish
  2731	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wonder on wonder, Wielder of Glory!
  2732	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2733	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I had given up all hope, when this brave liegeman came to our aid.}
  2734	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2735	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But lately I reckoned ne'er under heaven
  2736	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Comfort to gain me for any of sorrows,
  2737	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 While the handsomest of houses horrid with bloodstain
  2738	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gory uptowered; grief had offfrightened[3]
  2739	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Each of the wise ones who weened not that ever
  2740	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The folk-troop's defences 'gainst foes they should strengthen,
  2741	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Gainst sprites and monsters. Through the might of the Wielder
  2742	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 A doughty retainer hath a deed now accomplished
  2743	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which erstwhile we all with our excellent wisdom
  2744	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2745	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{If his mother yet liveth, well may she thank God for this son.}
  2746	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2747	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Failed to perform. May affirm very truly
  2748	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          What woman soever in all of the nations
  2749	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gave birth to the child, if yet she surviveth,
  2750	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 That the long-ruling Lord was lavish to herward
  2751	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the birth of the bairn. Now, Beowulf dear,
  2752	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2753	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hereafter, Beowulf, thou shalt be my son.}
  2754	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2755	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Most excellent hero, I'll love thee in spirit
  2756	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As bairn of my body; bear well henceforward
  2757	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The relationship new. No lack shall befall thee
  2758	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Of earth-joys any I ever can give thee.
  2759	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Full often for lesser service I've given
  2760	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[34]      Hero less hardy hoard-treasure precious,
  2761	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2762	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Thou hast won immortal distinction.}
  2763	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2764	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To a weaker in war-strife. By works of distinction
  2765	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thou hast gained for thyself now that thy glory shall flourish
  2766	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Forever and ever. The All-Ruler quite thee
  2767	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With good from His hand as He hitherto did thee!"
  2768	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2769	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf replies: I was most happy to render thee this service.}
  2770	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2771	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf answered, Ecgtheow's offspring:
  2772	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "That labor of glory most gladly achieved we,
  2773	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The combat accomplished, unquailing we ventured
  2774	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 The enemy's grapple; I would grant it much rather
  2775	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thou wert able to look at the creature in person,
  2776	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Faint unto falling, the foe in his trappings!
  2777	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On murder-bed quickly I minded to bind him,
  2778	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With firm-holding fetters, that forced by my grapple
  2779	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Low he should lie in life-and-death struggle
  2780	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Less his body escape; I was wholly unable,
  2781	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2782	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I could not keep the monster from escaping, as God did not will that I
  2783	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tshould.}
  2784	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2785	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since God did not will it, to keep him from going,
  2786	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not held him that firmly, hated opposer;
  2787	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Too swift was the foeman. Yet safety regarding
  2788	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 He suffered his hand behind him to linger,
  2789	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His arm and shoulder, to act as watcher;
  2790	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2791	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He left his hand and arm behind.}
  2792	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2793	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          No shadow of solace the woe-begone creature
  2794	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Found him there nathless: the hated destroyer
  2795	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Liveth no longer, lashed for his evils,
  2796	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 But sorrow hath seized him, in snare-meshes hath him
  2797	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Close in its clutches, keepeth him writhing
  2798	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In baleful bonds: there banished for evil
  2799	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The man shall wait for the mighty tribunal,
  2800	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2801	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{God will give him his deserts.}
  2802	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2803	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          How the God of glory shall give him his earnings."

  2805	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  2806	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Unferth has nothing more to say, for Beowulf's actions speak louder than
  2807	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\twords.}

  2809	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From boasting and bragging of battle-achievements,
  2810	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since the princes beheld there the hand that depended
  2811	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath the lofty hall-timbers by the might of the nobleman,
  2812	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Each one before him, the enemy's fingers;
  2813	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Each finger-nail strong steel most resembled,

  2815	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Claw most uncanny; quoth they agreeing,

  2817	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[35]

  2823	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Battle-hand bloody to bear away from him.

  2857	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Whole and uninjured when the horrible creature

  2894	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 He needed not blush for in battle-men's presence.

  2916	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 The famous one's valor ne'er failed at the front when

  2920	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In so manly a manner the mighty-famed chieftain,
  2921	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[37]   55 Hoard-ward of heroes, with horses and jewels

  3191	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] For 1130 (1) R. and Gr. suggest 'elne unflitme' as 1098 (1) reads.
  3192	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    The latter verse is undisputed; and, for the former, 'elne' would be
  3193	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    as possible as 'ealles,' and 'unflitme' is well supported. Accepting
  3194	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'elne unflitme' for both, I would suggest '_very peaceably_' for both
  3195	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    places: (1) _Finn to Hengest very peaceably vowed with oaths_, etc.
  3196	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (2) _Hengest then still the slaughter-stained winter remained there
  3197	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    with Finn very peaceably_. The two passages become thus correlatives,
  3198	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the second a sequel of the first. 'Elne,' in the sense of very
  3199	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (swíðe), needs no argument; and 'unflitme' (from 'flítan') can, it
  3200	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    seems to me, be more plausibly rendered 'peaceful,' 'peaceable,' than
  3201	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'contestable,' or 'conquerable.'
  3202	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3203	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] Some scholars have proposed 'roden'; the line would then read:
  3204	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    _Then the building was reddened, etc._, instead of 'covered.' The 'h'
  3205	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    may have been carried over from the three alliterating 'h's.'

  3210	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXIX.
  3211	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3212	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF RECEIVES FURTHER HONOR.
  3213	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3214	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3215	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{More gifts are offered Beowulf.}
  3216	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3217	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A beaker was borne him, and bidding to quaff it
  3218	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Graciously given, and gold that was twisted
  3219	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Pleasantly proffered, a pair of arm-jewels,
  3220	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[42]      Rings and corslet, of collars the greatest
  3221	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 I've heard of 'neath heaven. Of heroes not any
  3222	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          More splendid from jewels have I heard 'neath the welkin,
  3223	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3224	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A famous necklace is referred to, in comparison with the gems presented
  3225	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tto Beowulf.}
  3226	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3227	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since Hama off bore the Brosingmen's necklace,
  3228	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The bracteates and jewels, from the bright-shining city,[1]
  3229	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Eormenric's cunning craftiness fled from,
  3230	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Chose gain everlasting. Geatish Higelac,
  3231	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Grandson of Swerting, last had this jewel
  3232	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When tramping 'neath banner the treasure he guarded,
  3233	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The field-spoil defended; Fate offcarried him
  3234	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When for deeds of daring he endured tribulation,
  3235	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Hate from the Frisians; the ornaments bare he
  3236	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          O'er the cup of the currents, costly gem-treasures,
  3237	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mighty folk-leader, he fell 'neath his target;
  3238	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The[2] corpse of the king then came into charge of
  3239	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The race of the Frankmen, the mail-shirt and collar:
  3240	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Warmen less noble plundered the fallen,
  3241	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When the fight was finished; the folk of the Geatmen
  3242	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The field of the dead held in possession.
  3243	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The choicest of mead-halls with cheering resounded.
  3244	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wealhtheo discoursed, the war-troop addressed she:
  3245	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3246	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Queen Wealhtheow magnifies Beowulf's achievements.}
  3247	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3248	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 "This collar enjoy thou, Beowulf worthy,
  3249	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Young man, in safety, and use thou this armor,
  3250	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gems of the people, and prosper thou fully,
  3251	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Show thyself sturdy and be to these liegemen
  3252	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mild with instruction! I'll mind thy requital.
  3253	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Thou hast brought it to pass that far and near
  3254	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Forever and ever earthmen shall honor thee,
  3255	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Even so widely as ocean surroundeth
  3256	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The blustering bluffs. Be, while thou livest,
  3257	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[43]      A wealth-blessèd atheling. I wish thee most truly
  3258	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3259	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{May gifts never fail thee.}
  3260	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3261	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Jewels and treasure. Be kind to my son, thou
  3262	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Living in joyance! Here each of the nobles
  3263	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Is true unto other, gentle in spirit,
  3264	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Loyal to leader. The liegemen are peaceful,
  3265	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The war-troops ready: well-drunken heroes,[3]
  3266	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Do as I bid ye." Then she went to the settle.
  3267	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          There was choicest of banquets, wine drank the heroes:
  3268	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3269	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{They little know of the sorrow in store for them.}
  3270	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3271	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Weird they knew not, destiny cruel,
  3272	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As to many an earlman early it happened,
  3273	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When evening had come and Hrothgar had parted
  3274	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Off to his manor, the mighty to slumber.
  3275	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Warriors unnumbered warded the building
  3276	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As erst they did often: the ale-settle bared they,
  3277	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas covered all over with beds and pillows.
  3278	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3279	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A doomed thane is there with them.}
  3280	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3281	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Doomed unto death, down to his slumber
  3282	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Bowed then a beer-thane. Their battle-shields placed they,
  3283	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bright-shining targets, up by their heads then;
  3284	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          O'er the atheling on ale-bench 'twas easy to see there
  3285	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Battle-high helmet, burnie of ring-mail,
  3286	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3287	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{They were always ready for battle.}
  3288	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3289	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And mighty war-spear. 'Twas the wont of that people
  3290	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 To constantly keep them equipped for the battle,[4]
  3291	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          At home or marching--in either condition--
  3292	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          At seasons just such as necessity ordered
  3293	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As best for their ruler; that people was worthy.
  3294	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3295	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] C. suggests a semicolon after 'city,' with 'he' as supplied
  3296	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    subject of 'fled' and 'chose.'
  3297	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3298	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] For 'feorh' S. suggests 'feoh': 'corpse' in the translation would
  3299	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    then be changed to '_possessions_,' '_belongings_.' This is a better
  3300	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    reading than one joining, in such intimate syntactical relations,
  3301	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    things so unlike as 'corpse' and 'jewels.'
  3302	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3303	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] S. suggests '_wine-joyous heroes_,' '_warriors elated with wine_.'
  3304	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3305	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [4] I believe this translation brings out the meaning of the poet,
  3306	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    without departing seriously from the H.-So. text. 'Oft' frequently
  3307	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    means 'constantly,' 'continually,' not always 'often.'--Why 'an (on)
  3308	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    wíg gearwe' should be written 'ánwíg-gearwe' (= ready for single
  3309	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    combat), I cannot see. 'Gearwe' occurs quite frequently with 'on'; cf.
  3310	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    B. 1110 (_ready for the pyre_), El. 222 (_ready for the glad
  3311	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    journey_). Moreover, what has the idea of single combat to do with B.
  3312	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    1247 ff.? The poet is giving an inventory of the arms and armor which
  3313	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    they lay aside on retiring, and he closes his narration by saying that
  3314	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    they were _always prepared for battle both at home and on the march_.

  3323	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tTHE MOTHER OF GRENDEL.
  3324	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3325	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3326	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They sank then to slumber. With sorrow one paid for
  3327	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His evening repose, as often betid them
  3328	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          While Grendel was holding[1] the gold-bedecked palace,
  3329	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ill-deeds performing, till his end overtook him,
  3330	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Death for his sins. 'Twas seen very clearly,
  3331	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3332	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Grendel's mother is known to be thirsting for revenge.}
  3333	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3334	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Known unto earth-folk, that still an avenger
  3335	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Outlived the loathed one, long since the sorrow
  3336	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Caused by the struggle; the mother of Grendel,
  3337	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Devil-shaped woman, her woe ever minded,
  3338	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Who was held to inhabit the horrible waters,
  3339	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3340	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{[Grendel's progenitor, Cain, is again referred to.]}
  3341	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3342	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The cold-flowing currents, after Cain had become a
  3343	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Slayer-with-edges to his one only brother,
  3344	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The son of his sire; he set out then banished,
  3345	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Marked as a murderer, man-joys avoiding,
  3346	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Lived in the desert. Thence demons unnumbered
  3347	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3348	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The poet again magnifies Beowulf's valor.}
  3349	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3350	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fate-sent awoke; one of them Grendel,
  3351	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sword-cursèd, hateful, who at Heorot met with
  3352	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A man that was watching, waiting the struggle,
  3353	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Where a horrid one held him with hand-grapple sturdy;
  3354	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Nathless he minded the might of his body,
  3355	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The glorious gift God had allowed him,
  3356	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And folk-ruling Father's favor relied on,
  3357	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His help and His comfort: so he conquered the foeman,
  3358	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hell-spirit humbled: he unhappy departed then,
  3359	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Reaved of his joyance, journeying to death-haunts,
  3360	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Foeman of man. His mother moreover
  3361	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3362	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Grendel's mother comes to avenge her son.}
  3363	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3364	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Eager and gloomy was anxious to go on
  3365	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Her mournful mission, mindful of vengeance
  3366	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For the death of her son. She came then to Heorot
  3367	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[45]   30 Where the Armor-Dane earlmen all through the building
  3368	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Were lying in slumber. Soon there became then
  3369	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Return[2] to the nobles, when the mother of Grendel
  3370	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Entered the folk-hall; the fear was less grievous
  3371	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By even so much as the vigor of maidens,
  3372	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 War-strength of women, by warrior is reckoned,
  3373	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When well-carved weapon, worked with the hammer,
  3374	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Blade very bloody, brave with its edges,
  3375	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Strikes down the boar-sign that stands on the helmet.
  3376	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the hard-edgèd weapon was heaved in the building,[3]
  3377	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 The brand o'er the benches, broad-lindens many
  3378	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hand-fast were lifted; for helmet he recked not,
  3379	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For armor-net broad, whom terror laid hold of.
  3380	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          She went then hastily, outward would get her
  3381	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Her life for to save, when some one did spy her;
  3382	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3383	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{She seizes a favorite liegemen of Hrothgar's.}
  3384	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3385	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Soon she had grappled one of the athelings
  3386	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fast and firmly, when fenward she hied her;
  3387	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That one to Hrothgar was liefest of heroes
  3388	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In rank of retainer where waters encircle,
  3389	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A mighty shield-warrior, whom she murdered at slumber,
  3390	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 A broadly-famed battle-knight. Beowulf was absent,
  3391	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3392	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf was asleep in another part of the palace.}
  3393	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3394	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But another apartment was erstwhile devoted
  3395	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the glory-decked Geatman when gold was distributed.
  3396	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          There was hubbub in Heorot. The hand that was famous
  3397	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          She grasped in its gore;[4] grief was renewed then
  3398	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[46]   55 In homes and houses: 'twas no happy arrangement
  3399	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In both of the quarters to barter and purchase
  3400	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With lives of their friends. Then the well-agèd ruler,
  3401	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The gray-headed war-thane, was woful in spirit,
  3402	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When his long-trusted liegeman lifeless he knew of,
  3403	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3404	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is sent for.}
  3405	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3406	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 His dearest one gone. Quick from a room was
  3407	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf brought, brave and triumphant.
  3408	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As day was dawning in the dusk of the morning,
  3409	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3410	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He comes at Hrothgar's summons.}
  3411	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3412	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Went then that earlman, champion noble,
  3413	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Came with comrades, where the clever one bided
  3414	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Whether God all gracious would grant him a respite
  3415	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          After the woe he had suffered. The war-worthy hero
  3416	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With a troop of retainers trod then the pavement
  3417	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          (The hall-building groaned), till he greeted the wise one,
  3418	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  3420	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3421	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The earl of the Ingwins;[5] asked if the night had
  3422	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 Fully refreshed him, as fain he would have it.

  3425	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    make this verse read, _While Grendel was wasting the gold-bedecked
  3426	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    palace_. So 20_15 below: _ravaged the desert_.

  3437	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    as an emendation with (?) to v. 739, he offers, because 'under'
  3438	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    baffles him in both passages. All we need is to take 'under' in its
  3439	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    secondary meaning of 'in,' which, though not given by Grein, occurs in

  3442	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    such circumstances,' which interchanges in good usage with 'under such
  3443	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    circumstances.'

  3454	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tHROTHGAR'S ACCOUNT OF THE MONSTERS.

  3459	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hrothgar rejoined, helm of the Scyldings:

  3462	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Yrmenlaf's brother, older than he,
  3463	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 My true-hearted counsellor, trusty adviser,
  3464	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Shoulder-companion, when fighting in battle
  3465	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Our heads we protected, when troopers were clashing,
  3466	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3467	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He was my ideal hero.}
  3468	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3469	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And heroes were dashing; such an earl should be ever,
  3470	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          An erst-worthy atheling, as Æschere proved him.
  3471	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 The flickering death-spirit became in Heorot
  3472	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His hand-to-hand murderer; I can not tell whither
  3473	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The cruel one turned in the carcass exulting,
  3474	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3475	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[47]
  3476	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3477	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{This horrible creature came to avenge Grendel's death.}
  3478	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3479	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By cramming discovered.[1] The quarrel she wreaked then,
  3480	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That last night igone Grendel thou killedst
  3481	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 In grewsomest manner, with grim-holding clutches,
  3482	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since too long he had lessened my liege-troop and wasted
  3483	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My folk-men so foully. He fell in the battle
  3484	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With forfeit of life, and another has followed,
  3485	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A mighty crime-worker, her kinsman avenging,
  3486	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 And henceforth hath 'stablished her hatred unyielding,[2]
  3487	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As it well may appear to many a liegeman,
  3488	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who mourneth in spirit the treasure-bestower,
  3489	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Her heavy heart-sorrow; the hand is now lifeless
  3490	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which[3] availed you in every wish that you cherished.
  3491	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3492	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I have heard my vassals speak of these two uncanny monsters who lived in
  3493	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tthe moors.}
  3494	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3495	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Land-people heard I, liegemen, this saying,
  3496	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Dwellers in halls, they had seen very often
  3497	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A pair of such mighty march-striding creatures,
  3498	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Far-dwelling spirits, holding the moorlands:
  3499	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          One of them wore, as well they might notice,
  3500	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 The image of woman, the other one wretched
  3501	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In guise of a man wandered in exile,
  3502	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Except he was huger than any of earthmen;
  3503	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Earth-dwelling people entitled him Grendel
  3504	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In days of yore: they know not their father,
  3505	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Whe'r ill-going spirits any were borne him
  3506	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3507	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The inhabit the most desolate and horrible places.}
  3508	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3509	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ever before. They guard the wolf-coverts,
  3510	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lands inaccessible, wind-beaten nesses,
  3511	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fearfullest fen-deeps, where a flood from the mountains
  3512	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath mists of the nesses netherward rattles,
  3513	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 The stream under earth: not far is it henceward
  3514	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Measured by mile-lengths that the mere-water standeth,
  3515	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which forests hang over, with frost-whiting covered,[4]
  3516	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[48]      A firm-rooted forest, the floods overshadow.
  3517	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          There ever at night one an ill-meaning portent
  3518	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 A fire-flood may see; 'mong children of men
  3519	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          None liveth so wise that wot of the bottom;
  3520	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though harassed by hounds the heath-stepper seek for,
  3521	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3522	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Even the hounded deer will not seek refuge in these uncanny regions.}
  3523	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3524	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fly to the forest, firm-antlered he-deer,
  3525	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Spurred from afar, his spirit he yieldeth,
  3526	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 His life on the shore, ere in he will venture
  3527	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To cover his head. Uncanny the place is:
  3528	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thence upward ascendeth the surging of waters,
  3529	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wan to the welkin, when the wind is stirring
  3530	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The weathers unpleasing, till the air groweth gloomy,
  3531	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3532	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{To thee only can I look for assistance.}
  3533	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3534	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 And the heavens lower. Now is help to be gotten
  3535	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From thee and thee only! The abode thou know'st not,
  3536	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The dangerous place where thou'rt able to meet with
  3537	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The sin-laden hero: seek if thou darest!
  3538	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For the feud I will fully fee thee with money,
  3539	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 With old-time treasure, as erstwhile I did thee,
  3540	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With well-twisted jewels, if away thou shalt get thee."
  3541	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  3560	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF SEEKS GRENDEL'S MOTHER.

  3562	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3563	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf answered, Ecgtheow's son:
  3564	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3565	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf exhorts the old king to arouse himself for action.}
  3566	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3567	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Grieve not, O wise one! for each it is better,
  3568	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His friend to avenge than with vehemence wail him;
  3569	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Each of us must the end-day abide of
  3570	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 His earthly existence; who is able accomplish
  3571	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Glory ere death! To battle-thane noble
  3572	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lifeless lying, 'tis at last most fitting.
  3573	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Arise, O king, quick let us hasten
  3574	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To look at the footprint of the kinsman of Grendel!
  3575	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 I promise thee this now: to his place he'll escape not,
  3576	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To embrace of the earth, nor to mountainous forest,
  3577	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nor to depths of the ocean, wherever he wanders.
  3578	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[49]      Practice thou now patient endurance
  3579	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of each of thy sorrows, as I hope for thee soothly!"
  3580	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3581	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar rouses himself. His horse is brought.}

  3583	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Then up sprang the old one, the All-Wielder thanked he,
  3584	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ruler Almighty, that the man had outspoken.

  3587	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3588	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{They start on the track of the female monster.}
  3589	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  3591	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Of linden-wood bearers. Her footprints were seen then
  3592	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Widely in wood-paths, her way o'er the bottoms,
  3593	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Where she faraway fared o'er fen-country murky,
  3594	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bore away breathless the best of retainers
  3595	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who pondered with Hrothgar the welfare of country.
  3596	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 The son of the athelings then went o'er the stony,
  3597	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Declivitous cliffs, the close-covered passes,
  3598	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Narrow passages, paths unfrequented,
  3599	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nesses abrupt, nicker-haunts many;
  3600	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          One of a few of wise-mooded heroes,
  3601	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 He onward advanced to view the surroundings,
  3602	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Till he found unawares woods of the mountain
  3603	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          O'er hoar-stones hanging, holt-wood unjoyful;
  3604	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The water stood under, welling and gory.
  3605	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas irksome in spirit to all of the Danemen,
  3606	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Friends of the Scyldings, to many a liegeman
  3607	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  3609	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3610	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sad to be suffered, a sorrow unlittle
  3611	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To each of the earlmen, when to Æschere's head they
  3612	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Came on the cliff. The current was seething
  3613	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With blood and with gore (the troopers gazed on it).
  3614	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 The horn anon sang the battle-song ready.
  3615	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The troop were all seated; they saw 'long the water then
  3616	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3617	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The water is filled with serpents and sea-dragons.}
  3618	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3619	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Many a serpent, mere-dragons wondrous
  3620	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Trying the waters, nickers a-lying
  3621	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On the cliffs of the nesses, which at noonday full often

  3624	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3625	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{One of them is killed by Beowulf.}
  3626	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3627	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hot-mooded, hateful, they heard the great clamor,
  3628	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The war-trumpet winding. One did the Geat-prince
  3629	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[50]      Sunder from earth-joys, with arrow from bowstring,
  3630	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 From his sea-struggle tore him, that the trusty war-missile
  3631	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3632	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dead beast is a poor swimmer}
  3633	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  3636	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Soon in the waters the wonderful swimmer
  3637	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was straitened most sorely with sword-pointed boar-spears,
  3638	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Pressed in the battle and pulled to the cliff-edge;
  3639	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The liegemen then looked on the loath-fashioned stranger.
  3640	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3641	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf prepares for a struggle with the monster.}
  3642	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3643	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf donned then his battle-equipments,
  3644	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Cared little for life; inlaid and most ample,
  3645	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hand-woven corslet which could cover his body,
  3646	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Must the wave-deeps explore, that war might be powerless
  3647	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To harm the great hero, and the hating one's grasp might
  3648	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not peril his safety; his head was protected
  3649	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By the light-flashing helmet that should mix with the bottoms,
  3650	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Trying the eddies, treasure-emblazoned,
  3651	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Encircled with jewels, as in seasons long past
  3652	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The weapon-smith worked it, wondrously made it,
  3653	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With swine-bodies fashioned it, that thenceforward no longer
  3654	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Brand might bite it, and battle-sword hurt it.

  3658	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3659	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 That Hrothgar's spokesman had lent him when straitened;

  3666	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The battle-field sought; not the earliest occasion

  3683	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXIII.
  3684	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3685	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF'S FIGHT WITH GRENDEL'S MOTHER.

  3687	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3688	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf makes a parting speech to Hrothgar.}
  3689	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3690	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf spake, Ecgtheow's son:
  3691	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Recall now, oh, famous kinsman of Healfdene,
  3692	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Prince very prudent, now to part I am ready,
  3693	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gold-friend of earlmen, what erst we agreed on,
  3694	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3695	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{If I fail, act as a kind liegelord to my thanes,}
  3696	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3697	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Should I lay down my life in lending thee assistance,
  3698	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When my earth-joys were over, thou wouldst evermore serve me
  3699	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In stead of a father; my faithful thanemen,
  3700	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My trusty retainers, protect thou and care for,
  3701	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fall I in battle: and, Hrothgar belovèd,
  3702	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  3706	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thou to me hast allotted. The lord of the Geatmen
  3707	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          May perceive from the gold, the Hrethling may see it
  3708	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  3711	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When he looks on the jewels, that a gem-giver found I
  3712	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Good over-measure, enjoyed him while able.
  3713	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 And the ancient heirloom Unferth permit thou,
  3714	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The famed one to have, the heavy-sword splendid[1]
  3715	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hard-edgèd weapon; with Hrunting to aid me,
  3716	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I shall gain me glory, or grim-death shall take me."

  3721	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Heroic did hasten, not any rejoinder
  3722	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was willing to wait for; the wave-current swallowed
  3723	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  3736	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Some one of men from above was exploring.

  3762	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3763	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 The mighty mere-woman; he made a great onset

  3765	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From striking, that war-blade struck on her head then
