  3767	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3768	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The sword will not bite.}
  3769	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3770	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The sword would not bite, her life would not injure,
  3771	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 But the falchion failed the folk-prince when straitened:
  3772	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Erst had it often onsets encountered,
  3773	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Oft cloven the helmet, the fated one's armor:
  3774	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas the first time that ever the excellent jewel
  3775	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had failed of its fame. Firm-mooded after,
  3776	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Not heedless of valor, but mindful of glory,
  3777	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was Higelac's kinsman; the hero-chief angry
  3778	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Cast then his carved-sword covered with jewels
  3779	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That it lay on the earth, hard and steel-pointed;
  3780	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3781	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The hero throws down all weapons, and again trusts to his hand-grip.}
  3782	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3783	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He hoped in his strength, his hand-grapple sturdy.
  3784	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 So any must act whenever he thinketh
  3785	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To gain him in battle glory unending,
  3786	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And is reckless of living. The lord of the War-Geats
  3787	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[53]      (He shrank not from battle) seized by the shoulder[2]
  3788	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The mother of Grendel; then mighty in struggle
  3789	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Swung he his enemy, since his anger was kindled,
  3790	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That she fell to the floor. With furious grapple
  3791	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3792	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf falls.}
  3793	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3794	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          She gave him requital[3] early thereafter,
  3795	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And stretched out to grab him; the strongest of warriors
  3796	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Faint-mooded stumbled, till he fell in his traces,
  3797	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3798	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The monster sits on him with drawn sword.}
  3799	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3800	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 Foot-going champion. Then she sat on the hall-guest
  3801	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And wielded her war-knife wide-bladed, flashing,
  3802	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For her son would take vengeance, her one only bairn.
  3803	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3804	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{His armor saves his life.}
  3805	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3806	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His breast-armor woven bode on his shoulder;
  3807	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          It guarded his life, the entrance defended
  3808	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 'Gainst sword-point and edges. Ecgtheow's son there
  3809	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had fatally journeyed, champion of Geatmen,
  3810	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the arms of the ocean, had the armor not given,
  3811	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Close-woven corslet, comfort and succor,
  3812	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3813	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{God arranged for his escape.}
  3814	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3815	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And had God most holy not awarded the victory,
  3816	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 All-knowing Lord; easily did heaven's
  3817	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ruler most righteous arrange it with justice;[4]
  3818	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Uprose he erect ready for battle.

  3839	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF IS DOUBLE-CONQUEROR.
  3840	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3841	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3842	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf grasps a giant-sword,}
  3843	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3844	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then he saw mid the war-gems a weapon of victory,
  3845	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          An ancient giant-sword, of edges a-doughty,
  3846	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Glory of warriors: of weapons 'twas choicest,
  3847	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Only 'twas larger than any man else was
  3848	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[54]    5 Able to bear to the battle-encounter,
  3849	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The good and splendid work of the giants.
  3850	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He grasped then the sword-hilt, knight of the Scyldings,
  3851	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bold and battle-grim, brandished his ring-sword,
  3852	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hopeless of living, hotly he smote her,
  3853	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 That the fiend-woman's neck firmly it grappled,
  3854	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3855	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{and fells the female monster.}
  3856	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3857	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Broke through her bone-joints, the bill fully pierced her
  3858	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fate-cursèd body, she fell to the ground then:
  3859	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hand-sword was bloody, the hero exulted.
  3860	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The brand was brilliant, brightly it glimmered,
  3861	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Just as from heaven gemlike shineth
  3862	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The torch of the firmament. He glanced 'long the building,
  3863	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And turned by the wall then, Higelac's vassal
  3864	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Raging and wrathful raised his battle-sword
  3865	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Strong by the handle. The edge was not useless
  3866	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 To the hero-in-battle, but he speedily wished to
  3867	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Give Grendel requital for the many assaults he
  3868	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had worked on the West-Danes not once, but often,
  3869	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When he slew in slumber the subjects of Hrothgar,
  3870	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Swallowed down fifteen sleeping retainers
  3871	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Of the folk of the Danemen, and fully as many
  3872	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Carried away, a horrible prey.
  3873	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He gave him requital, grim-raging champion,
  3874	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3875	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf sees the body of Grendel, and cuts off his head.}
  3876	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3877	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When he saw on his rest-place weary of conflict
  3878	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Grendel lying, of life-joys bereavèd,
  3879	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 As the battle at Heorot erstwhile had scathed him;
  3880	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His body far bounded, a blow when he suffered,
  3881	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Death having seized him, sword-smiting heavy,
  3882	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And he cut off his head then. Early this noticed
  3883	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The clever carles who as comrades of Hrothgar
  3884	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3885	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The waters are gory.}
  3886	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3887	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Gazed on the sea-deeps, that the surging wave-currents
  3888	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Were mightily mingled, the mere-flood was gory:
  3889	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the good one the gray-haired together held converse,
  3890	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3891	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is given up for dead.}
  3892	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3893	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hoary of head, that they hoped not to see again
  3894	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The atheling ever, that exulting in victory
  3895	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 He'd return there to visit the distinguished folk-ruler:
  3896	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[55]      Then many concluded the mere-wolf had killed him.[1]
  3897	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ninth hour came then. From the ness-edge departed
  3898	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The bold-mooded Scyldings; the gold-friend of heroes
  3899	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Homeward betook him. The strangers sat down then
  3900	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Soul-sick, sorrowful, the sea-waves regarding:
  3901	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They wished and yet weened not their well-loved friend-lord
  3902	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3903	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The giant-sword melts.}
  3904	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3905	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To see any more. The sword-blade began then,
  3906	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The blood having touched it, contracting and shriveling
  3907	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With battle-icicles; 'twas a wonderful marvel
  3908	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 That it melted entirely, likest to ice when
  3909	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Father unbindeth the bond of the frost and
  3910	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Unwindeth the wave-bands, He who wieldeth dominion
  3911	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of times and of tides: a truth-firm Creator.
  3912	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nor took he of jewels more in the dwelling,
  3913	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Lord of the Weders, though they lay all around him,
  3914	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Than the head and the handle handsome with jewels;
  3915	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[56]      The brand early melted, burnt was the weapon:[2]
  3916	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So hot was the blood, the strange-spirit poisonous
  3917	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3918	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The hero swims back to the realms of day.}
  3919	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3920	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That in it did perish. He early swam off then
  3921	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Who had bided in combat the carnage of haters,
  3922	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Went up through the ocean; the eddies were cleansèd,
  3923	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The spacious expanses, when the spirit from farland
  3924	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His life put aside and this short-lived existence.
  3925	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The seamen's defender came swimming to land then
  3926	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Doughty of spirit, rejoiced in his sea-gift,
  3927	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The bulky burden which he bore in his keeping.
  3928	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The excellent vassals advanced then to meet him,
  3929	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To God they were grateful, were glad in their chieftain,
  3930	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That to see him safe and sound was granted them.
  3931	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 From the high-minded hero, then, helmet and burnie
  3932	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Were speedily loosened: the ocean was putrid,
  3933	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The water 'neath welkin weltered with gore.
  3934	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Forth did they fare, then, their footsteps retracing,
  3935	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Merry and mirthful, measured the earth-way,
  3936	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 The highway familiar: men very daring[3]
  3937	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bare then the head from the sea-cliff, burdening
  3938	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Each of the earlmen, excellent-valiant.
  3939	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3940	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{It takes four men to carry Grendel's head on a spear.}
  3941	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3942	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Four of them had to carry with labor
  3943	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The head of Grendel to the high towering gold-hall
  3944	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 Upstuck on the spear, till fourteen most-valiant
  3945	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And battle-brave Geatmen came there going
  3946	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Straight to the palace: the prince of the people
  3947	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Measured the mead-ways, their mood-brave companion.
  3948	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The atheling of earlmen entered the building,
  3949	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       85 Deed-valiant man, adorned with distinction,
  3950	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Doughty shield-warrior, to address King Hrothgar:
  3951	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[57]      Then hung by the hair, the head of Grendel
  3952	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was borne to the building, where beer-thanes were drinking,
  3953	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Loth before earlmen and eke 'fore the lady:
  3954	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       90 The warriors beheld then a wonderful sight.
  3955	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3956	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] 'Þæs monige gewearð' (1599) and 'hafað þæs geworden' (2027).--In a
  3957	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    paper published some years ago in one of the Johns Hopkins University
  3958	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    circulars, I tried to throw upon these two long-doubtful passages some
  3959	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    light derived from a study of like passages in Alfred's prose.--The
  3960	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    impersonal verb 'geweorðan,' with an accus. of the person, and a
  3961	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    þæt-clause is used several times with the meaning 'agree.' See Orosius
  3962	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (Sweet's ed.) 178_7; 204_34; 208_28; 210_15; 280_20. In the two
  3963	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Beowulf passages, the þæt-clause is anticipated by 'þæs,' which is
  3964	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    clearly a gen. of the thing agreed on.
  3965	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3966	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    The first passage (v. 1599 (b)-1600) I translate literally: _Then many
  3967	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    agreed upon this (namely), that the sea-wolf had killed him_.
  3968	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3969	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    The second passage (v. 2025 (b)-2027): _She is promised ...; to this
  3970	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the friend of the Scyldings has agreed, etc_. By emending 'is' instead
  3971	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    of 'wæs' (2025), the tenses will be brought into perfect harmony.
  3972	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3973	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    In v. 1997 ff. this same idiom occurs, and was noticed in B.'s great
  3974	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    article on Beowulf, which appeared about the time I published my
  3975	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    reading of 1599 and 2027. Translate 1997 then: _Wouldst let the
  3976	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    South-Danes themselves decide about their struggle with Grendel_. Here
  3977	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'Súð-Dene' is accus. of person, and 'gúðe' is gen. of thing agreed on.
  3978	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3979	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    With such collateral support as that afforded by B. (P. and B. XII.
  3980	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    97), I have no hesitation in departing from H.-So., my usual guide.
  3981	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3982	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    The idiom above treated runs through A.-S., Old Saxon, and other
  3983	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Teutonic languages, and should be noticed in the lexicons.
  3984	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3985	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] 'Bróden-mæl' is regarded by most scholars as meaning a damaskeened
  3986	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    sword. Translate: _The damaskeened sword burned up_. Cf. 25_16 and
  3987	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    note.
  3988	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  3989	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] 'Cyning-balde' (1635) is the much-disputed reading of K. and Th.
  3990	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    To render this, "_nobly bold_," "_excellently bold_," have been
  3991	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    suggested. B. would read 'cyning-holde' (cf. 290), and render: _Men
  3992	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    well-disposed towards the king carried the head, etc._ 'Cynebealde,'
  3993	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    says t.B., endorsing Gr.

  4000	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF BRINGS HIS TROPHIES.--HROTHGAR'S GRATITUDE.
  4001	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4002	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4003	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf relates his last exploit.}
  4004	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4005	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf spake, offspring of Ecgtheow:
  4006	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Lo! we blithely have brought thee, bairn of Healfdene,
  4007	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Prince of the Scyldings, these presents from ocean
  4008	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which thine eye looketh on, for an emblem of glory.
  4009	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 I came off alive from this, narrowly 'scaping:
  4010	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In war 'neath the water the work with great pains I
  4011	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Performed, and the fight had been finished quite nearly,
  4012	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had God not defended me. I failed in the battle
  4013	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Aught to accomplish, aided by Hrunting,
  4014	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Though that weapon was worthy, but the Wielder of earth-folk
  4015	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4016	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{God was fighting with me.}
  4017	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4018	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gave me willingly to see on the wall a
  4019	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Heavy old hand-sword hanging in splendor
  4020	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          (He guided most often the lorn and the friendless),
  4021	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That I swung as a weapon. The wards of the house then
  4022	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 I killed in the conflict (when occasion was given me).
  4023	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the battle-sword burned, the brand that was lifted,[1]
  4024	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As the blood-current sprang, hottest of war-sweats;
  4025	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Seizing the hilt, from my foes I offbore it;
  4026	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I avenged as I ought to their acts of malignity,
  4027	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 The murder of Danemen. I then make thee this promise,
  4028	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4029	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Heorot is freed from monsters.}
  4030	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4031	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thou'lt be able in Heorot careless to slumber
  4032	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With thy throng of heroes and the thanes of thy people
  4033	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Every and each, of greater and lesser,
  4034	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And thou needest not fear for them from the selfsame direction
  4035	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 As thou formerly fearedst, oh, folk-lord of Scyldings,
  4036	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[58]     End-day for earlmen." To the age-hoary man then,
  4037	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4038	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The famous sword is presented to Hrothgar.}
  4039	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4040	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The gray-haired chieftain, the gold-fashioned sword-hilt,
  4041	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Old-work of giants, was thereupon given;
  4042	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since the fall of the fiends, it fell to the keeping
  4043	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Of the wielder of Danemen, the wonder-smith's labor,
  4044	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And the bad-mooded being abandoned this world then,
  4045	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Opponent of God, victim of murder,
  4046	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And also his mother; it went to the keeping
  4047	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the best of the world-kings, where waters encircle,
  4048	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Who the scot divided in Scylding dominion.
  4049	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4050	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar looks closely at the old sword.}
  4051	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4052	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hrothgar discoursed, the hilt he regarded,
  4053	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ancient heirloom where an old-time contention's
  4054	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beginning was graven: the gurgling currents,
  4055	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The flood slew thereafter the race of the giants,
  4056	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 They had proved themselves daring: that people was loth to
  4057	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4058	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{It had belonged to a race hateful to God.}
  4059	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4060	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Lord everlasting, through lash of the billows
  4061	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Father gave them final requital.
  4062	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So in letters of rune on the clasp of the handle
  4063	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gleaming and golden, 'twas graven exactly,
  4064	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Set forth and said, whom that sword had been made for,
  4065	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Finest of irons, who first it was wrought for,
  4066	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wreathed at its handle and gleaming with serpents.
  4067	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The wise one then said (silent they all were)
  4068	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4069	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar praises Beowulf.}
  4070	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4071	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Son of old Healfdene: "He may say unrefuted
  4072	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Who performs 'mid the folk-men fairness and truth
  4073	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          (The hoary old ruler remembers the past),
  4074	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That better by birth is this bairn of the nobles!
  4075	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thy fame is extended through far-away countries,
  4076	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Good friend Beowulf, o'er all of the races,
  4077	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Thou holdest all firmly, hero-like strength with
  4078	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Prudence of spirit. I'll prove myself grateful
  4079	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As before we agreed on; thou granted for long shalt
  4080	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Become a great comfort to kinsmen and comrades,
  4081	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4082	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Heremod's career is again contrasted with Beowulf's.}
  4083	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4084	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A help unto heroes. Heremod became not
  4085	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Such to the Scyldings, successors of Ecgwela;
  4086	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He grew not to please them, but grievous destruction,
  4087	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[59]      And diresome death-woes to Danemen attracted;
  4088	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He slew in anger his table-companions,
  4089	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Trustworthy counsellors, till he turned off lonely
  4090	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 From world-joys away, wide-famous ruler:
  4091	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though high-ruling heaven in hero-strength raised him,
  4092	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In might exalted him, o'er men of all nations
  4093	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Made him supreme, yet a murderous spirit
  4094	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Grew in his bosom: he gave then no ring-gems
  4095	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4096	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A wretched failure of a king, to give no jewels to his retainers.}
  4097	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4098	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 To the Danes after custom; endured he unjoyful
  4099	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Standing the straits from strife that was raging,
  4100	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Longsome folk-sorrow. Learn then from this,
  4101	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lay hold of virtue! Though laden with winters,
  4102	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I have sung thee these measures. 'Tis a marvel to tell it,
  4103	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4104	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar moralizes.}
  4105	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4106	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 How all-ruling God from greatness of spirit
  4107	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Giveth wisdom to children of men,
  4108	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Manor and earlship: all things He ruleth.
  4109	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He often permitteth the mood-thought of man of
  4110	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The illustrious lineage to lean to possessions,
  4111	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 Allows him earthly delights at his manor,
  4112	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A high-burg of heroes to hold in his keeping,
  4113	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Maketh portions of earth-folk hear him,
  4114	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And a wide-reaching kingdom so that, wisdom failing him,
  4115	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He himself is unable to reckon its boundaries;
  4116	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       85 He liveth in luxury, little debars him,
  4117	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nor sickness nor age, no treachery-sorrow
  4118	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Becloudeth his spirit, conflict nowhere,
  4119	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          No sword-hate, appeareth, but all of the world doth
  4120	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wend as he wisheth; the worse he knoweth not,
  4121	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       90 Till arrant arrogance inward pervading,
  4122	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Waxeth and springeth, when the warder is sleeping,
  4123	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The guard of the soul: with sorrows encompassed,
  4124	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Too sound is his slumber, the slayer is near him,
  4125	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who with bow and arrow aimeth in malice.
  4126	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  4136	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4137	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tHROTHGAR MORALIZES.--REST AFTER LABOR.
  4138	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4139	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4140	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A wounded spirit.}
  4141	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4142	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Then bruised in his bosom he with bitter-toothed missile
  4143	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Is hurt 'neath his helmet: from harmful pollution
  4144	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He is powerless to shield him by the wonderful mandates
  4145	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the loath-cursèd spirit; what too long he hath holden
  4146	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Him seemeth too small, savage he hoardeth,
  4147	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Nor boastfully giveth gold-plated rings,[1]
  4148	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The fate of the future flouts and forgetteth
  4149	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since God had erst given him greatness no little,
  4150	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wielder of Glory. His end-day anear,
  4151	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 It afterward happens that the bodily-dwelling
  4152	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fleetingly fadeth, falls into ruins;
  4153	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Another lays hold who doleth the ornaments,
  4154	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The nobleman's jewels, nothing lamenting,
  4155	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Heedeth no terror. Oh, Beowulf dear,
  4156	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Best of the heroes, from bale-strife defend thee,
  4157	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And choose thee the better, counsels eternal;
  4158	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4159	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Be not over proud: life is fleeting, and its strength soon wasteth away.}
  4160	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4161	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beware of arrogance, world-famous champion!
  4162	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But a little-while lasts thy life-vigor's fulness;
  4163	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twill after hap early, that illness or sword-edge
  4164	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Shall part thee from strength, or the grasp of the fire,
  4165	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Or the wave of the current, or clutch of the edges,
  4166	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Or flight of the war-spear, or age with its horrors,
  4167	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Or thine eyes' bright flashing shall fade into darkness:
  4168	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twill happen full early, excellent hero,
  4169	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4170	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar gives an account of his reign.}
  4171	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4172	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 That death shall subdue thee. So the Danes a half-century
  4173	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I held under heaven, helped them in struggles
  4174	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Gainst many a race in middle-earth's regions,
  4175	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With ash-wood and edges, that enemies none
  4176	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On earth molested me. Lo! offsetting change, now,
  4177	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4178	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[61]
  4179	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4180	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Sorrow after joy.}
  4181	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4182	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Came to my manor, grief after joyance,
  4183	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When Grendel became my constant visitor,
  4184	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Inveterate hater: I from that malice
  4185	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Continually travailed with trouble no little.
  4186	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thanks be to God that I gained in my lifetime,
  4187	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 To the Lord everlasting, to look on the gory
  4188	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Head with mine eyes, after long-lasting sorrow!
  4189	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Go to the bench now, battle-adornèd
  4190	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Joy in the feasting: of jewels in common
  4191	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          We'll meet with many when morning appeareth."
  4192	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 The Geatman was gladsome, ganged he immediately
  4193	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To go to the bench, as the clever one bade him.
  4194	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then again as before were the famous-for-prowess,
  4195	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hall-inhabiters, handsomely banqueted,
  4196	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Feasted anew. The night-veil fell then
  4197	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Dark o'er the warriors. The courtiers rose then;
  4198	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The gray-haired was anxious to go to his slumbers,
  4199	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hoary old Scylding. Hankered the Geatman,
  4200	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4201	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf is fagged, and seeks rest.}
  4202	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4203	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The champion doughty, greatly, to rest him:
  4204	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          An earlman early outward did lead him,
  4205	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Fagged from his faring, from far-country springing,
  4206	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who for etiquette's sake all of a liegeman's
  4207	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Needs regarded, such as seamen at that time
  4208	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Were bounden to feel. The big-hearted rested;
  4209	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The building uptowered, spacious and gilded,
  4210	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 The guest within slumbered, till the sable-clad raven
  4211	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Blithely foreboded the beacon of heaven.
  4212	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the bright-shining sun o'er the bottoms came going;[2]
  4213	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The warriors hastened, the heads of the peoples
  4214	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Were ready to go again to their peoples,
  4215	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4216	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The Geats prepare to leave Dane-land.}
  4217	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4218	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 The high-mooded farer would faraway thenceward
  4219	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Look for his vessel. The valiant one bade then,[3]
  4220	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  4224	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4225	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Offspring of Ecglaf, off to bear Hrunting,
  4226	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To take his weapon, his well-beloved iron;

  4228	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 The war-friend and mighty, nor chid he with words then

  4254	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4255	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tSORROW AT PARTING.
  4256	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4257	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4258	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf's farewell.}
  4259	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4260	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf spake, Ecgtheow's offspring:
  4261	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "We men of the water wish to declare now
  4262	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fared from far-lands, we're firmly determined
  4263	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To seek King Higelac. Here have we fitly
  4264	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Been welcomed and feasted, as heart would desire it;
  4265	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Good was the greeting. If greater affection
  4266	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I am anywise able ever on earth to
  4267	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gain at thy hands, ruler of heroes,
  4268	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Than yet I have done, I shall quickly be ready
  4269	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4270	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I shall be ever ready to aid thee.}
  4271	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4272	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 For combat and conflict. O'er the course of the waters
  4273	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Learn I that neighbors alarm thee with terror,
  4274	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As haters did whilom, I hither will bring thee
  4275	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For help unto heroes henchmen by thousands.
  4276	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4277	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{My liegelord will encourage me in aiding thee.}
  4278	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4279	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I know as to Higelac, the lord of the Geatmen,
  4280	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Though young in years, he yet will permit me,
  4281	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By words and by works, ward of the people,
  4282	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fully to furnish thee forces and bear thee
  4283	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My lance to relieve thee, if liegemen shall fail thee,
  4284	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And help of my hand-strength; if Hrethric be treating,
  4285	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[63]   20 Bairn of the king, at the court of the Geatmen,
  4286	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He thereat may find him friends in abundance:
  4287	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Faraway countries he were better to seek for
  4288	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who trusts in himself." Hrothgar discoursed then,
  4289	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Making rejoinder: "These words thou hast uttered
  4290	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 All-knowing God hath given thy spirit!
  4291	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4292	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{O Beowulf, thou art wise beyond thy years.}
  4293	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4294	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ne'er heard I an earlman thus early in life
  4295	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          More clever in speaking: thou'rt cautious of spirit,
  4296	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mighty of muscle, in mouth-answers prudent.
  4297	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I count on the hope that, happen it ever
  4298	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 That missile shall rob thee of Hrethel's descendant,
  4299	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Edge-horrid battle, and illness or weapon
  4300	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Deprive thee of prince, of people's protector,
  4301	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4302	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Should Higelac die, the Geats could find no better successor than thou
  4303	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\twouldst make.}
  4304	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4305	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And life thou yet holdest, the Sea-Geats will never
  4306	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Find a more fitting folk-lord to choose them,
  4307	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Gem-ward of heroes, than _thou_ mightest prove thee,
  4308	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          If the kingdom of kinsmen thou carest to govern.
  4309	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thy mood-spirit likes me the longer the better,
  4310	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf dear: thou hast brought it to pass that
  4311	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To both these peoples peace shall be common,
  4312	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4313	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Thou hast healed the ancient breach between our races.}
  4314	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4315	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 To Geat-folk and Danemen, the strife be suspended,
  4316	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The secret assailings they suffered in yore-days;
  4317	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And also that jewels be shared while I govern
  4318	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The wide-stretching kingdom, and that many shall visit
  4319	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Others o'er the ocean with excellent gift-gems:
  4320	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 The ring-adorned bark shall bring o'er the currents
  4321	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Presents and love-gifts. This people I know
  4322	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Tow'rd foeman and friend firmly established,[1]
  4323	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          After ancient etiquette everywise blameless."
  4324	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the warden of earlmen gave him still farther,
  4325	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4326	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Parting gifts}
  4327	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4328	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Kinsman of Healfdene, a dozen of jewels,
  4329	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bade him safely seek with the presents
  4330	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His well-beloved people, early returning.
  4331	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4332	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[64]
  4333	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4334	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar kisses Beowulf, and weeps.}
  4335	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4336	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the noble-born king kissed the distinguished,
  4337	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Dear-lovèd liegeman, the Dane-prince saluted him,
  4338	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 And claspèd his neck; tears from him fell,
  4339	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From the gray-headed man: he two things expected,
  4340	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Agèd and reverend, but rather the second,
  4341	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          [2]That bold in council they'd meet thereafter.
  4342	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The man was so dear that he failed to suppress the
  4343	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Emotions that moved him, but in mood-fetters fastened
  4344	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4345	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The old king is deeply grieved to part with his benefactor.}
  4346	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4347	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The long-famous hero longeth in secret
  4348	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Deep in his spirit for the dear-beloved man
  4349	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though not a blood-kinsman. Beowulf thenceward,
  4350	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gold-splendid warrior, walked o'er the meadows
  4351	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Exulting in treasure: the sea-going vessel
  4352	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Riding at anchor awaited its owner.
  4353	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As they pressed on their way then, the present of Hrothgar
  4354	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4355	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Giving liberally is the true proof of kingship.}
  4356	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4357	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was frequently referred to: a folk-king indeed that
  4358	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Everyway blameless, till age did debar him
  4359	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 The joys of his might, which hath many oft injured.
  4360	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4361	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] For 'geworhte,' the crux of this passage, B. proposes 'geþóhte,'
  4362	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    rendering: _I know this people with firm thought every way blameless
  4363	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    towards foe and friends_.

  4365	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] S. and B. emend so as to negative the verb 'meet.' "Why should

  4368	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the tears may have been due to many emotions, especially gratitude,
  4369	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    struggling for expression.

  4375	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4376	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tTHE HOMEWARD JOURNEY.--THE TWO QUEENS.
  4377	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4378	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4379	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the band of very valiant retainers
  4380	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Came to the current; they were clad all in armor,
  4381	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4382	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The coast-guard again.}
  4383	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4384	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In link-woven burnies. The land-warder noticed
  4385	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The return of the earlmen, as he erstwhile had seen them;
  4386	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Nowise with insult he greeted the strangers
  4387	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From the naze of the cliff, but rode on to meet them;
  4388	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Said the bright-armored visitors[1] vesselward traveled
  4389	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[65]      Welcome to Weders. The wide-bosomed craft then
  4390	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lay on the sand, laden with armor,
  4391	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 With horses and jewels, the ring-stemmèd sailer:
  4392	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The mast uptowered o'er the treasure of Hrothgar.
  4393	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4394	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf gives the guard a handsome sword.}
  4395	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4396	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the boat-ward a gold-bound brand he presented,
  4397	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That he was afterwards honored on the ale-bench more highly
  4398	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As the heirloom's owner. [2]Set he out on his vessel,
  4399	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 To drive on the deep, Dane-country left he.
  4400	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Along by the mast then a sea-garment fluttered,
  4401	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A rope-fastened sail. The sea-boat resounded,
  4402	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The wind o'er the waters the wave-floater nowise
  4403	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Kept from its journey; the sea-goer traveled,
  4404	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 The foamy-necked floated forth o'er the currents,
  4405	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The well-fashioned vessel o'er the ways of the ocean,
  4406	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4407	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The Geats see their own land again.}
  4408	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4409	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Till they came within sight of the cliffs of the Geatmen,
  4410	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The well-known headlands. The wave-goer hastened
  4411	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Driven by breezes, stood on the shore.
  4412	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4413	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The port-warden is anxiously looking for them.}
  4414	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4415	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Prompt at the ocean, the port-ward was ready,
  4416	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who long in the past outlooked in the distance,[3]
  4417	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          At water's-edge waiting well-lovèd heroes;
  4418	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He bound to the bank then the broad-bosomed vessel
  4419	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fast in its fetters, lest the force of the waters
  4420	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Should be able to injure the ocean-wood winsome.
  4421	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bade he up then take the treasure of princes,
  4422	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Plate-gold and fretwork; not far was it thence
  4423	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To go off in search of the giver of jewels:
  4424	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[66]      Hrethel's son Higelac at home there remaineth,[4]
  4425	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Himself with his comrades close to the sea-coast.
  4426	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The building was splendid, the king heroic,
  4427	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Great in his hall, Hygd very young was,
  4428	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4429	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hygd, the noble queen of Higelac, lavish of gifts.}
  4430	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4431	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fine-mooded, clever, though few were the winters
  4432	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That the daughter of Hæreth had dwelt in the borough;
  4433	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 But she nowise was cringing nor niggard of presents,
  4434	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of ornaments rare, to the race of the Geatmen.
  4435	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4436	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Offa's consort, Thrytho, is contrasted with Hygd.}
  4437	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4438	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thrytho nursed anger, excellent[5] folk-queen,
  4439	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hot-burning hatred: no hero whatever
  4440	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Mong household companions, her husband excepted
  4441	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4442	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{She is a terror to all save her husband.}
  4443	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4444	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Dared to adventure to look at the woman
  4445	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With eyes in the daytime;[6] but he knew that death-chains
  4446	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hand-wreathed were wrought him: early thereafter,
  4447	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When the hand-strife was over, edges were ready,
  4448	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That fierce-raging sword-point had to force a decision,
  4449	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Murder-bale show. Such no womanly custom
  4450	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For a lady to practise, though lovely her person,
  4451	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That a weaver-of-peace, on pretence of anger
  4452	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A belovèd liegeman of life should deprive.
  4453	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Soothly this hindered Heming's kinsman;
  4454	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Other ale-drinking earlmen asserted
  4455	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That fearful folk-sorrows fewer she wrought them,
  4456	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Treacherous doings, since first she was given
  4457	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Adorned with gold to the war-hero youthful,
  4458	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For her origin honored, when Offa's great palace
  4459	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 O'er the fallow flood by her father's instructions
  4460	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          She sought on her journey, where she afterwards fully,
  4461	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Famed for her virtue, her fate on the king's-seat
  4462	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[67]      Enjoyed in her lifetime, love did she hold with
  4463	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ruler of heroes, the best, it is told me,
  4464	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Of all of the earthmen that oceans encompass,
  4465	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of earl-kindreds endless; hence Offa was famous
  4466	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Far and widely, by gifts and by battles,
  4467	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Spear-valiant hero; the home of his fathers
  4468	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He governed with wisdom, whence Eomær did issue
  4469	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 For help unto heroes, Heming's kinsman,
  4470	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Grandson of Garmund, great in encounters.
  4471	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4472	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] For 'scawan' (1896), 'scaðan' has been proposed. Accepting this,
  4473	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    we may render: _He said the bright-armored warriors were going to
  4474	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    their vessel, welcome, etc_. (Cf. 1804.)
  4475	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4476	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] R. suggests, 'Gewát him on naca,' and renders: _The vessel set
  4477	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    out, to drive on the sea, the Dane-country left_. 'On' bears the
  4478	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    alliteration; cf. 'on hafu' (2524). This has some advantages over the
  4479	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    H.-So. reading; viz. (1) It adds nothing to the text; (2) it makes
  4480	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'naca' the subject, and thus brings the passage into keeping with the
  4481	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    context, where the poet has exhausted his vocabulary in detailing the
  4482	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    actions of the vessel.--B.'s emendation (cf. P. and B. XII. 97) is
  4483	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    violent.
  4484	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4485	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] B. translates: _Who for a long time, ready at the coast, had
  4486	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    looked out into the distance eagerly for the dear men_. This changes
  4487	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the syntax of 'léofra manna.'
  4488	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4489	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [4] For 'wunað' (v. 1924) several eminent critics suggest 'wunade'
  4490	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (=remained). This makes the passage much clearer.
  4491	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4492	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [5] Why should such a woman be described as an 'excellent' queen? C.
  4493	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    suggests 'frécnu' = dangerous, bold.
  4494	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4495	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [6] For 'an dæges' various readings have been offered. If 'and-éges'
  4496	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    be accepted, the sentence will read: _No hero ... dared look upon her,
  4497	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    eye to eye_. If 'án-dæges' be adopted, translate: _Dared look upon her
  4498	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the whole day_.

  4523	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The building was early inward made ready
  4524	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For the foot-going guests as the good one had ordered.

  4538	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  4542	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the high-towering palace. A curious interest
  4543	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Tormented his spirit, what meaning to see in
  4544	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 The Sea-Geats' adventures: "Beowulf worthy,

  4547	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  4549	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Far o'er the salt-streams to seek an encounter,
  4550	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A battle at Heorot? Hast bettered for Hrothgar,
  4551	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The famous folk-leader, his far-published sorrows

  4553	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  4557	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the belovèd liegeman; I long time did pray thee
  4558	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By no means to seek out the murderous spirit,

  4560	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Grappling with Grendel. To God I am thankful
  4561	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To be suffered to see thee safe from thy journey."
  4562	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  4564	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4565	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf answered, bairn of old Ecgtheow:
  4566	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "'Tis hidden by no means, Higelac chieftain,
  4567	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From many of men, the meeting so famous,
  4568	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 What mournful moments of me and of Grendel
  4569	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Were passed in the place where he pressing affliction
  4570	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On the Victory-Scyldings scathefully brought,
  4571	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Anguish forever; that all I avengèd,
  4572	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So that any under heaven of the kinsmen of Grendel
  4573	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  4575	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  4577	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who longest liveth of the loth-going kindred,[3]
  4578	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Encompassed by moorland. I came in my journey
  4579	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the royal ring-hall, Hrothgar to greet there:
  4580	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  4582	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  4585	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Assign me a seat with the son of his bosom.
  4586	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[69]      The troop was in joyance; mead-glee greater
  4587	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath arch of the ether not ever beheld I
  4588	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  4592	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Peace-tie of peoples, oft passed through the building,
  4593	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Cheered the young troopers; she oft tendered a hero
  4594	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A beautiful ring-band, ere she went to her sitting.
  4595	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4596	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrothgar's lovely daughter.}
  4597	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4598	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Oft the daughter of Hrothgar in view of the courtiers
  4599	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the earls at the end the ale-vessel carried,
  4600	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Whom Freaware I heard then hall-sitters title,
  4601	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When nail-adorned jewels she gave to the heroes:
  4602	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4603	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{She is betrothed to Ingeld, in order to unite the Danes and Heathobards.}
  4604	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4605	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gold-bedecked, youthful, to the glad son of Froda
  4606	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Her faith has been plighted; the friend of the Scyldings,
  4607	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The guard of the kingdom, hath given his sanction,[4]
  4608	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 And counts it a vantage, for a part of the quarrels,
  4609	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A portion of hatred, to pay with the woman.
  4610	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          [5]Somewhere not rarely, when the ruler has fallen,
  4611	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The life-taking lance relaxeth its fury
  4612	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For a brief breathing-spell, though the bride be charming!
  4613	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4614	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] 'Meodu-scencum' (1981) some would render '_with mead-pourers_.'
  4615	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Translate then: _The daughter of Hæreth went through the building
  4616	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    accompanied by mead-pourers_.
  4617	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4618	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] See my note to 1599, supra, and B. in P. and B. XII. 97.
  4619	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4620	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] For 'fenne,' supplied by Grdtvg., B. suggests 'fácne' (cf. Jul.
  4621	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    350). Accepting this, translate: _Who longest lives of the hated race,
  4622	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    steeped in treachery_.
  4623	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4624	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [4] See note to v. 1599 above.
  4625	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4626	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [5] This is perhaps the least understood sentence in the poem, almost
  4627	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    every word being open to dispute. (1) The 'nó' of our text is an
  4628	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    emendation, and is rejected by many scholars. (2) 'Seldan' is by some
  4629	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    taken as an adv. (= _seldom_), and by others as a noun (= _page_,
  4630	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    _companion_). (3) 'Léod-hryre,' some render '_fall of the people_';
  4631	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    others, '_fall of the prince_.' (4) 'Búgeð,' most scholars regard as
  4632	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the intrans. verb meaning '_bend_,' '_rest_'; but one great scholar has
  4633	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    translated it '_shall kill_.' (5) 'Hwær,' Very recently, has been
  4634	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    attacked, 'wære' being suggested. (6) As a corollary to the above, the
  4635	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    same critic proposes to drop 'oft' out of the text.--t.B. suggests: Oft
  4636	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    seldan wære after léodhryre: lýtle hwíle bongár búgeð, þéah séo brýd
  4637	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    duge = _often has a treaty been (thus) struck, after a prince had
  4638	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    fallen: (but only) a short time is the spear (then) wont to rest,
  4639	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    however excellent the bride may be_.

  4646	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF NARRATES HIS ADVENTURES TO HIGELAC.
  4647	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4648	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4649	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "It well may discomfit the prince of the Heathobards
  4650	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And each of the thanemen of earls that attend him,
  4651	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[70]      When he goes to the building escorting the woman,
  4652	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That a noble-born Daneman the knights should be feasting:
  4653	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 There gleam on his person the leavings of elders
  4654	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hard and ring-bright, Heathobards' treasure,
  4655	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          While they wielded their arms, till they misled to the battle
  4656	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Their own dear lives and belovèd companions.
  4657	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He saith at the banquet who the collar beholdeth,
  4658	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 An ancient ash-warrior who earlmen's destruction
  4659	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Clearly recalleth (cruel his spirit),
  4660	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sadly beginneth sounding the youthful
  4661	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thane-champion's spirit through the thoughts of his bosom,
  4662	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          War-grief to waken, and this word-answer speaketh:
  4663	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4664	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Ingeld is stirred up to break the truce.}
  4665	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4666	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 'Art thou able, my friend, to know when thou seest it
  4667	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The brand which thy father bare to the conflict
  4668	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In his latest adventure, 'neath visor of helmet,
  4669	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The dearly-loved iron, where Danemen did slay him,
  4670	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And brave-mooded Scyldings, on the fall of the heroes,
  4671	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 (When vengeance was sleeping) the slaughter-place wielded?
  4672	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          E'en now some man of the murderer's progeny
  4673	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Exulting in ornaments enters the building,
  4674	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Boasts of his blood-shedding, offbeareth the jewel
  4675	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which thou shouldst wholly hold in possession!'
  4676	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 So he urgeth and mindeth on every occasion
  4677	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With woe-bringing words, till waxeth the season
  4678	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When the woman's thane for the works of his father,
  4679	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The bill having bitten, blood-gory sleepeth,
  4680	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fated to perish; the other one thenceward
  4681	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 'Scapeth alive, the land knoweth thoroughly.[1]
  4682	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the oaths of the earlmen on each side are broken,
  4683	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When rancors unresting are raging in Ingeld
  4684	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And his wife-love waxeth less warm after sorrow.
  4685	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So the Heathobards' favor not faithful I reckon,
  4686	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Their part in the treaty not true to the Danemen,
  4687	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Their friendship not fast. I further shall tell thee
  4688	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4689	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[71]
  4690	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4691	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Having made these preliminary statements, I will now tell thee of
  4692	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tGrendel, the monster.}
  4693	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4694	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          More about Grendel, that thou fully mayst hear,
  4695	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ornament-giver, what afterward came from
  4696	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hand-rush of heroes. When heaven's bright jewel
  4697	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 O'er earthfields had glided, the stranger came raging,
  4698	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The horrible night-fiend, us for to visit,
  4699	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Where wholly unharmed the hall we were guarding.
  4700	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4701	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hondscio fell first}
  4702	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4703	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To Hondscio happened a hopeless contention,
  4704	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Death to the doomed one, dead he fell foremost,
  4705	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Girded war-champion; to him Grendel became then,
  4706	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the vassal distinguished, a tooth-weaponed murderer,
  4707	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The well-beloved henchman's body all swallowed.
  4708	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not the earlier off empty of hand did
  4709	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The bloody-toothed murderer, mindful of evils,
  4710	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Wish to escape from the gold-giver's palace,
  4711	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But sturdy of strength he strove to outdo me,
  4712	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hand-ready grappled. A glove was suspended
  4713	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Spacious and wondrous, in art-fetters fastened,
  4714	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which was fashioned entirely by touch of the craftman
  4715	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 From the dragon's skin by the devil's devices:
  4716	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He down in its depths would do me unsadly
  4717	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          One among many, deed-doer raging,
  4718	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though sinless he saw me; not so could it happen
  4719	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When I in my anger upright did stand.
  4720	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 'Tis too long to recount how requital I furnished
  4721	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For every evil to the earlmen's destroyer;
  4722	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4723	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I reflected honor upon my people.}
  4724	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4725	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas there, my prince, that I proudly distinguished
  4726	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Thy land with my labors. He left and retreated,
  4727	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He lived his life a little while longer:
  4728	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Yet his right-hand guarded his footstep in Heorot,
  4729	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And sad-mooded thence to the sea-bottom fell he,
  4730	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mournful in mind. For the might-rush of battle
  4731	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4732	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{King Hrothgar lavished gifts upon me.}
  4733	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4734	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The friend of the Scyldings, with gold that was plated,
  4735	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With ornaments many, much requited me,
  4736	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 When daylight had dawned, and down to the banquet
  4737	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          We had sat us together. There was chanting and joyance:
  4738	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The age-stricken Scylding asked many questions
  4739	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[72]      And of old-times related; oft light-ringing harp-strings,

  4741	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 Now he uttered measures, mourning and truthful,
  4742	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the large-hearted land-king a legend of wonder
  4743	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Truthfully told us. Now troubled with years
  4744	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  4746	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4747	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The age-hoary warrior afterward began to
  4748	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mourn for the might that marked him in youth-days;
  4749	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 His breast within boiled, when burdened with winters
  4750	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Much he remembered. From morning till night then
  4751	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          We joyed us therein as etiquette suffered,

  4867	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Slew not carousing; his mood was not cruel,

  4881	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The heirloom of Hrethel, embellished with gold,

  4888	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Seven of thousands, manor and lordship.
  4889	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Common to both was land 'mong the people,
  4890	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[75]      Estate and inherited rights and possessions,
  4891	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the second one specially spacious dominions,
  4892	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the one who was better. It afterward happened
  4893	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 In days that followed, befell the battle-thanes,

  4901	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Of Hereric in battle. To Beowulf's keeping
  4902	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Turned there in time extensive dominions:
  4903	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  4944	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tTHE HOARD AND THE DRAGON.

  4946	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4947	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          *       *       *       *       *       *       *
  4948	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He sought of himself who sorely did harm him,
  4949	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But, for need very pressing, the servant of one of
  4950	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The sons of the heroes hate-blows evaded,
  4951	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Seeking for shelter and the sin-driven warrior
  4952	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Took refuge within there. He early looked in it,
  4953	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          *       *       *       *       *       *       *
  4954	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          *       *       *       *       *       *       *
  4955	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[76]      *  *  *  *  *  * when the onset surprised him,
  4956	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4957	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The hoard.}
  4958	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4959	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 He a gem-vessel saw there: many of suchlike
  4960	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ancient ornaments in the earth-cave were lying,
  4961	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As in days of yore some one of men of
  4962	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Illustrious lineage, as a legacy monstrous,
  4963	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          There had secreted them, careful and thoughtful,
  4964	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Dear-valued jewels. Death had offsnatched them,
  4965	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the days of the past, and the one man moreover
  4966	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the flower of the folk who fared there the longest,
  4967	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was fain to defer it, friend-mourning warder,
  4968	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A little longer to be left in enjoyment
  4969	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 Of long-lasting treasure.[1] A barrow all-ready
  4970	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Stood on the plain the stream-currents nigh to,
  4971	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          New by the ness-edge, unnethe of approaching:
  4972	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The keeper of rings carried within a
  4973	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          [2]Ponderous deal of the treasure of nobles,
  4974	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Of gold that was beaten, briefly he spake then:[3]
  4975	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4976	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The ring-giver bewails the loss of retainers.}
  4977	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  4978	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "Hold thou, O Earth, now heroes no more may,
  4979	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The earnings of earlmen. Lo! erst in thy bosom
  4980	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Worthy men won them; war-death hath ravished,
  4981	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Perilous life-bale, all my warriors,
  4982	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Liegemen belovèd, who this life have forsaken,
  4983	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who hall-pleasures saw. No sword-bearer have I,
  4984	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And no one to burnish the gold-plated vessel,
  4985	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The high-valued beaker: my heroes are vanished.
  4986	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hardy helmet behung with gilding
  4987	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Shall be reaved of its riches: the ring-cleansers slumber
  4988	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who were charged to have ready visors-for-battle,
  4989	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And the burnie that bided in battle-encounter
  4990	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[77]      O'er breaking of war-shields the bite of the edges
  4991	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Moulds with the hero. The ring-twisted armor,
  4992	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Its lord being lifeless, no longer may journey
  4993	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hanging by heroes; harp-joy is vanished,
  4994	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The rapture of glee-wood, no excellent falcon
  4995	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Swoops through the building, no swift-footed charger
  4996	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Grindeth the gravel. A grievous destruction
  4997	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 No few of the world-folk widely hath scattered!"
  4998	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So, woful of spirit one after all
  4999	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lamented mournfully, moaning in sadness
  5000	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By day and by night, till death with its billows
  5001	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5002	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The fire-dragon}
  5003	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5004	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Dashed on his spirit. Then the ancient dusk-scather
  5005	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Found the great treasure standing all open,
  5006	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He who flaming and fiery flies to the barrows,
  5007	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Naked war-dragon, nightly escapeth
  5008	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Encompassed with fire; men under heaven
  5009	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Widely beheld him. 'Tis said that he looks for[4]
  5010	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 The hoard in the earth, where old he is guarding
  5011	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The heathenish treasure; he'll be nowise the better.
  5012	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5013	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dragon meets his match.}
  5014	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5015	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So three-hundred winters the waster of peoples
  5016	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Held upon earth that excellent hoard-hall,
  5017	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Till the forementioned earlman angered him bitterly:

  5019	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And fullest remission for all his remissness
  5020	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Begged of his liegelord. Then the hoard[5] was discovered,
  5021	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The treasure was taken, his petition was granted
  5022	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  5025	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The lorn-mooded liegeman. His lord regarded
  5026	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 The old-work of earth-folk--'twas the earliest occasion.

  5029	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[78]      The footprint of foeman; too far had he gone

  5031	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 The fire-spewing dragon. So undoomed he may 'scape from

  5092	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBRAVE THOUGH AGED.--REMINISCENCES.

  5095	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dragon spits fire.}

  5097	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The stranger began then to vomit forth fire,
  5098	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To burn the great manor; the blaze then glimmered
  5099	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For anguish to earlmen, not anything living
  5100	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[79]      Was the hateful air-goer willing to leave there.
  5101	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 The war of the worm widely was noticed,
  5102	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The feud of the foeman afar and anear,
  5103	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          How the enemy injured the earls of the Geatmen,
  5104	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Harried with hatred: back he hied to the treasure,
  5105	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the well-hidden cavern ere the coming of daylight.
  5106	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 He had circled with fire the folk of those regions,
  5107	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With brand and burning; in the barrow he trusted,
  5108	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the wall and his war-might: the weening deceived him.
  5109	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5110	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf hears of the havoc wrought by the dragon.}
  5111	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5112	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then straight was the horror to Beowulf published,
  5113	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Early forsooth, that his own native homestead,[1]
  5114	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 The best of buildings, was burning and melting,
  5115	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gift-seat of Geatmen. 'Twas a grief to the spirit
  5116	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the good-mooded hero, the greatest of sorrows:
  5117	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5118	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He fears that Heaven is punishing him for some crime.}
  5119	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5120	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The wise one weened then that wielding his kingdom
  5121	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Gainst the ancient commandments, he had bitterly angered
  5122	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 The Lord everlasting: with lorn meditations
  5123	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His bosom welled inward, as was nowise his custom.
  5124	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The fire-spewing dragon fully had wasted
  5125	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The fastness of warriors, the water-land outward,
  5126	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The manor with fire. The folk-ruling hero,
  5127	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Prince of the Weders, was planning to wreak him.
  5128	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The warmen's defender bade them to make him,
  5129	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Earlmen's atheling, an excellent war-shield
  5130	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
