  5132	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5133	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wholly of iron: fully he knew then
  5134	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That wood from the forest was helpless to aid him,
  5135	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Shield against fire. The long-worthy ruler
  5136	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Must live the last of his limited earth-days,
  5137	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of life in the world and the worm along with him,
  5138	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though he long had been holding hoard-wealth in plenty.
  5139	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5140	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He determines to fight alone.}
  5141	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5142	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the ring-prince disdained to seek with a war-band,
  5143	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 With army extensive, the air-going ranger;
  5144	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He felt no fear of the foeman's assaults and
  5145	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He counted for little the might of the dragon,
  5146	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[80]      His power and prowess: for previously dared he
  5147	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5148	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf's early triumphs referred to}
  5149	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5150	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A heap of hostility, hazarded dangers,
  5151	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 War-thane, when Hrothgar's palace he cleansèd,
  5152	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Conquering combatant, clutched in the battle
  5153	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The kinsmen of Grendel, of kindred detested.[2]
  5154	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5155	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Higelac's death recalled.}
  5156	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5157	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas of hand-fights not least where Higelac was slaughtered,
  5158	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When the king of the Geatmen with clashings of battle,
  5159	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Friend-lord of folks in Frisian dominions,
  5160	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Offspring of Hrethrel perished through sword-drink,
  5161	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With battle-swords beaten; thence Beowulf came then
  5162	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          On self-help relying, swam through the waters;
  5163	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He bare on his arm, lone-going, thirty
  5164	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Outfits of armor, when the ocean he mounted.
  5165	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Hetwars by no means had need to be boastful
  5166	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of their fighting afoot, who forward to meet him
  5167	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Carried their war-shields: not many returned from
  5168	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The brave-mooded battle-knight back to their homesteads.
  5169	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Ecgtheow's bairn o'er the bight-courses swam then,
  5170	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Lone-goer lorn to his land-folk returning,
  5171	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Where Hygd to him tendered treasure and kingdom,
  5172	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5173	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Heardred's lack of capacity to rule.}
  5174	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5175	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Rings and dominion: her son she not trusted,
  5176	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To be able to keep the kingdom devised him
  5177	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 'Gainst alien races, on the death of King Higelac.
  5178	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5179	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf's tact and delicacy recalled.}
  5180	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5181	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Yet the sad ones succeeded not in persuading the atheling
  5182	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In any way ever, to act as a suzerain
  5183	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To Heardred, or promise to govern the kingdom;
  5184	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Yet with friendly counsel in the folk he sustained him,
  5185	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Gracious, with honor, till he grew to be older,
  5186	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5187	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Reference is here made to a visit which Beowulf receives from Eanmund and
  5188	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tEadgils, why they come is not known.}
  5189	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5190	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wielded the Weders. Wide-fleeing outlaws,
  5191	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ohthere's sons, sought him o'er the waters:
  5192	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They had stirred a revolt 'gainst the helm of the Scylfings,
  5193	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The best of the sea-kings, who in Swedish dominions
  5194	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 Distributed treasure, distinguished folk-leader.
  5195	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[81]      'Twas the end of his earth-days; injury fatal[3]
  5196	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By swing of the sword he received as a greeting,
  5197	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Offspring of Higelac; Ongentheow's bairn
  5198	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Later departed to visit his homestead,
  5199	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 When Heardred was dead; let Beowulf rule them,
  5200	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Govern the Geatmen: good was that folk-king.
  5201	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5202	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] 'Hám' (2326), the suggestion of B. is accepted by t.B. and other
  5203	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    scholars.
  5204	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5205	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] For 'láðan cynnes' (2355), t.B. suggests 'láðan cynne,' apposition
  5206	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    to 'mægum.' From syntactical and other considerations, this is a most
  5207	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    excellent emendation.

  5215	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXXIV.
  5216	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5217	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tBEOWULF SEEKS THE DRAGON.--BEOWULF'S REMINISCENCES.
  5218	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5219	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5220	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He planned requital for the folk-leader's ruin
  5221	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In days thereafter, to Eadgils the wretched
  5222	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Becoming an enemy. Ohthere's son then
  5223	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Went with a war-troop o'er the wide-stretching currents
  5224	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 With warriors and weapons: with woe-journeys cold he
  5225	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          After avenged him, the king's life he took.
  5226	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5227	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf has been preserved through many perils.}
  5228	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5229	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So he came off uninjured from all of his battles,
  5230	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Perilous fights, offspring of Ecgtheow,
  5231	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From his deeds of daring, till that day most momentous
  5232	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 When he fate-driven fared to fight with the dragon.
  5233	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5234	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{With eleven comrades, he seeks the dragon.}
  5235	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5236	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With eleven companions the prince of the Geatmen
  5237	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Went lowering with fury to look at the fire-drake:
  5238	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Inquiring he'd found how the feud had arisen,
  5239	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hate to his heroes; the highly-famed gem-vessel
  5240	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Was brought to his keeping through the hand of th' informer.
  5241	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5242	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{A guide leads the way, but}
  5243	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5244	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That in the throng was thirteenth of heroes,
  5245	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That caused the beginning of conflict so bitter,
  5246	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Captive and wretched, must sad-mooded thenceward
  5247	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5248	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{very reluctantly.}
  5249	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5250	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Point out the place: he passed then unwillingly
  5251	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 To the spot where he knew of the notable cavern,
  5252	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The cave under earth, not far from the ocean,
  5253	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The anger of eddies, which inward was full of
  5254	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Jewels and wires: a warden uncanny,
  5255	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[82]      Warrior weaponed, wardered the treasure,
  5256	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Old under earth; no easy possession
  5257	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For any of earth-folk access to get to.
  5258	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the battle-brave atheling sat on the naze-edge,
  5259	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          While the gold-friend of Geatmen gracious saluted
  5260	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His fireside-companions: woe was his spirit,
  5261	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Death-boding, wav'ring; Weird very near him,
  5262	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who must seize the old hero, his soul-treasure look for,
  5263	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Dragging aloof his life from his body:
  5264	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not flesh-hidden long was the folk-leader's spirit.
  5265	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf spake, Ecgtheow's son:
  5266	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5267	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf's retrospect.}
  5268	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5269	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 "I survived in my youth-days many a conflict,
  5270	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hours of onset: that all I remember.
  5271	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I was seven-winters old when the jewel-prince took me,
  5272	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          High-lord of heroes, at the hands of my father,
  5273	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hrethel the hero-king had me in keeping,
  5274	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5275	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrethel took me when I was seven.}
  5276	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5277	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Gave me treasure and feasting, our kinship remembered;
  5278	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not ever was I _any_ less dear to him
  5279	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5280	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He treated me as a son.}
  5281	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5282	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Knight in the boroughs, than the bairns of his household,
  5283	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Herebald and Hæthcyn and Higelac mine.
  5284	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the eldest unjustly by acts of a kinsman
  5285	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Was murder-bed strewn, since him Hæthcyn from horn-bow
  5286	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5287	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{One of the brothers accidentally kills another.}
  5288	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5289	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His sheltering chieftain shot with an arrow,
  5290	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Erred in his aim and injured his kinsman,
  5291	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          One brother the other, with blood-sprinkled spear:
  5292	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5293	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{No fee could compound for such a calamity.}
  5294	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5295	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas a feeless fight, finished in malice,
  5296	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Sad to his spirit; the folk-prince however
  5297	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had to part from existence with vengeance untaken.
  5298	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5299	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{[A parallel case is supposed.]}
  5300	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5301	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So to hoar-headed hero 'tis heavily crushing[1]
  5302	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[83]      To live to see his son as he rideth
  5303	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Young on the gallows: then measures he chanteth,
  5304	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 A song of sorrow, when his son is hanging
  5305	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For the raven's delight, and aged and hoary
  5306	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He is unable to offer any assistance.
  5307	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Every morning his offspring's departure
  5308	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Is constant recalled: he cares not to wait for
  5309	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 The birth of an heir in his borough-enclosures,
  5310	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since that one through death-pain the deeds hath experienced.
  5311	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He heart-grieved beholds in the house of his son the
  5312	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wine-building wasted, the wind-lodging places
  5313	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Reaved of their roaring; the riders are sleeping,
  5314	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 The knights in the grave; there's no sound of the harp-wood,
  5315	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Joy in the yards, as of yore were familiar.
  5316	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5317	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] 'Gomelum ceorle' (2445).--H. takes these words as referring to
  5318	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Hrethel; but the translator here departs from his editor by
  5319	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    understanding the poet to refer to a hypothetical old man, introduced
  5320	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    as an illustration of a father's sorrow.
  5321	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5322	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Hrethrel had certainly never seen a son of his ride on the gallows to
  5323	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    feed the crows.
  5324	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5325	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    The passage beginning 'swá bið géomorlic' seems to be an effort to
  5326	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    reach a full simile, 'as ... so.' 'As it is mournful for an old man,
  5327	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    etc. ... so the defence of the Weders (2463) bore heart-sorrow, etc.'
  5328	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    The verses 2451 to 2463-1/2 would be parenthetical, the poet's feelings
  5329	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    being so strong as to interrupt the simile. The punctuation of the
  5330	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    fourth edition would be better--a comma after 'galgan' (2447). The
  5331	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    translation may be indicated as follows: _(Just) as it is sad for an
  5332	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    old man to see his son ride young on the gallows when he himself is
  5333	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    uttering mournful measures, a sorrowful song, while his son hangs for a
  5334	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    comfort to the raven, and he, old and infirm, cannot render him any
  5335	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    kelp--(he is constantly reminded, etc., 2451-2463)--so the defence of
  5336	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the Weders, etc._

  5341	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tXXXV.
  5342	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5343	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tREMINISCENCES (_continued_).--BEOWULF'S LAST BATTLE.
  5344	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5345	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5346	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "He seeks then his chamber, singeth a woe-song
  5347	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          One for the other; all too extensive
  5348	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Seemed homesteads and plains. So the helm of the Weders
  5349	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5350	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hrethel grieves for Herebald.}
  5351	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5352	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mindful of Herebald heart-sorrow carried,
  5353	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Stirred with emotion, nowise was able
  5354	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To wreak his ruin on the ruthless destroyer:
  5355	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He was unable to follow the warrior with hatred,
  5356	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With deeds that were direful, though dear he not held him.
  5357	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[84]      Then pressed by the pang this pain occasioned him,
  5358	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 He gave up glee, God-light elected;
  5359	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He left to his sons, as the man that is rich does,
  5360	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His land and fortress, when from life he departed.
  5361	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5362	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Strife between Swedes and Geats.}
  5363	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5364	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then was crime and hostility 'twixt Swedes and Geatmen,
  5365	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          O'er wide-stretching water warring was mutual,
  5366	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Burdensome hatred, when Hrethel had perished,
  5367	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And Ongentheow's offspring were active and valiant,
  5368	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wished not to hold to peace oversea, but
  5369	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Round Hreosna-beorh often accomplished
  5370	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Cruelest massacre. This my kinsman avengèd,
  5371	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 The feud and fury, as 'tis found on inquiry,
  5372	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though one of them paid it with forfeit of life-joys,
  5373	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5374	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Hæthcyn's fall at Ravenswood.}
  5375	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5376	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With price that was hard: the struggle became then
  5377	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fatal to Hæthcyn, lord of the Geatmen.
  5378	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then I heard that at morning one brother the other
  5379	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 With edges of irons egged on to murder,
  5380	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Where Ongentheow maketh onset on Eofor:
  5381	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The helmet crashed, the hoary-haired Scylfing
  5382	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sword-smitten fell, his hand then remembered
  5383	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Feud-hate sufficient, refused not the death-blow.
  5384	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5385	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I requited him for the jewels he gave me.}
  5386	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5387	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 The gems that he gave me, with jewel-bright sword I
  5388	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Quited in contest, as occasion was offered:
  5389	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Land he allowed me, life-joy at homestead,
  5390	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Manor to live on. Little he needed
  5391	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          From Gepids or Danes or in Sweden to look for
  5392	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Trooper less true, with treasure to buy him;
  5393	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Mong foot-soldiers ever in front I would hie me,
  5394	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Alone in the vanguard, and evermore gladly
  5395	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Warfare shall wage, while this weapon endureth
  5396	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That late and early often did serve me
  5397	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5398	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf refers to his having slain Dæghrefn.}
  5399	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5400	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 When I proved before heroes the slayer of Dæghrefn,
  5401	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Knight of the Hugmen: he by no means was suffered
  5402	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the king of the Frisians to carry the jewels,
  5403	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The breast-decoration; but the banner-possessor
  5404	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bowed in the battle, brave-mooded atheling.
  5405	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[85]   45 No weapon was slayer, but war-grapple broke then
  5406	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The surge of his spirit, his body destroying.
  5407	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Now shall weapon's edge make war for the treasure,
  5408	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And hand and firm-sword." Beowulf spake then,
  5409	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Boast-words uttered--the latest occasion:
  5410	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5411	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He boasts of his youthful prowess, and declares himself still fearless.}
  5412	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5413	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 "I braved in my youth-days battles unnumbered;
  5414	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Still am I willing the struggle to look for,
  5415	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fame-deeds perform, folk-warden prudent,
  5416	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          If the hateful despoiler forth from his cavern
  5417	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Seeketh me out!" Each of the heroes,
  5418	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Helm-bearers sturdy, he thereupon greeted
  5419	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5420	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{His last salutations.}
  5421	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5422	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Belovèd co-liegemen--his last salutation:
  5423	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "No brand would I bear, no blade for the dragon,
  5424	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wist I a way my word-boast to 'complish[1]
  5425	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Else with the monster, as with Grendel I did it;
  5426	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 But fire in the battle hot I expect there,
  5427	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Furious flame-burning: so I fixed on my body
  5428	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Target and war-mail. The ward of the barrow[2]
  5429	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I'll not flee from a foot-length, the foeman uncanny.
  5430	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          At the wall 'twill befall us as Fate decreeth,
  5431	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5432	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Let Fate decide between us.}
  5433	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5434	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Each one's Creator. I am eager in spirit,
  5435	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With the wingèd war-hero to away with all boasting.
  5436	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bide on the barrow with burnies protected,
  5437	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5438	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wait ye here till the battle is over.}
  5439	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5440	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Earls in armor, which of _us_ two may better
  5441	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bear his disaster, when the battle is over.
  5442	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 'Tis no matter of yours, and man cannot do it,
  5443	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But me and me only, to measure his strength with
  5444	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The monster of malice, might-deeds to 'complish.
  5445	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I with prowess shall gain the gold, or the battle,
  5446	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[86]      Direful death-woe will drag off your ruler!"
  5447	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 The mighty champion rose by his shield then,
  5448	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Brave under helmet, in battle-mail went he
  5449	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath steep-rising stone-cliffs, the strength he relied on

  5452	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 Had lived through, most worthy, when foot-troops collided,

  5734	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Retained his consciousness, brandished his war-knife,
  5735	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Battle-sharp, bitter, that he bare on his armor:
  5736	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5737	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{and cuts the dragon.}
  5738	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5739	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The Weder-lord cut the worm in the middle.
  5740	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They had felled the enemy (life drove out then[3]
  5741	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Puissant prowess), the pair had destroyed him,
  5742	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Land-chiefs related: so a liegeman should prove him,
  5743	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A thaneman when needed. To the prince 'twas the last of
  5744	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His era of conquest by his own great achievements,
  5745	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5746	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[92]
  5747	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5748	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf's wound swells and burns.}
  5749	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5750	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The latest of world-deeds. The wound then began
  5751	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Which the earth-dwelling dragon erstwhile had wrought him
  5752	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 To burn and to swell. He soon then discovered
  5753	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That bitterest bale-woe in his bosom was raging,
  5754	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Poison within. The atheling advanced then,
  5755	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5756	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He sits down exhausted.}
  5757	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5758	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That along by the wall, he prudent of spirit
  5759	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Might sit on a settle; he saw the giant-work,
  5760	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 How arches of stone strengthened with pillars
  5761	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The earth-hall eternal inward supported.
  5762	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the long-worthy liegeman laved with his hand the
  5763	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5764	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf bathes his lord's head.}
  5765	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5766	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Far-famous chieftain, gory from sword-edge,
  5767	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Refreshing the face of his friend-lord and ruler,
  5768	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Sated with battle, unbinding his helmet.
  5769	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf answered, of his injury spake he,
  5770	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His wound that was fatal (he was fully aware
  5771	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He had lived his allotted life-days enjoying
  5772	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The pleasures of earth; then past was entirely
  5773	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 His measure of days, death very near):
  5774	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5775	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf regrets that he has no son.}
  5776	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5777	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          "My son I would give now my battle-equipments,
  5778	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Had any of heirs been after me granted,
  5779	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Along of my body. This people I governed
  5780	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fifty of winters: no king 'mong my neighbors
  5781	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Dared to encounter me with comrades-in-battle,
  5782	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Try me with terror. The time to me ordered
  5783	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I bided at home, mine own kept fitly,
  5784	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sought me no snares, swore me not many
  5785	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5786	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{I can rejoice in a well-spent life.}
  5787	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5788	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Oaths in injustice. Joy over all this
  5789	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 I'm able to have, though ill with my death-wounds;
  5790	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hence the Ruler of Earthmen need not charge me
  5791	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With the killing of kinsmen, when cometh my life out
  5792	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Forth from my body. Fare thou with haste now
  5793	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5794	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Bring me the hoard, Wiglaf, that my dying eyes may be refreshed by a
  5795	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tsight of it.}
  5796	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5797	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To behold the hoard 'neath the hoar-grayish stone,
  5798	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Well-lovèd Wiglaf, now the worm is a-lying,
  5799	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sore-wounded sleepeth, disseized of his treasure.
  5800	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Go thou in haste that treasures of old I,
  5801	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gold-wealth may gaze on, together see lying
  5802	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[93]      The ether-bright jewels, be easier able,
  5803	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Having the heap of hoard-gems, to yield my
  5804	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Life and the land-folk whom long I have governed."

  5806	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] B. renders: _He_ (_W_.) did not regard his (_the dragon's_) _head_
  5807	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (since Beowulf had struck it without effect), _but struck the dragon a
  5808	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    little lower down.--_One crux is to find out _whose head_ is meant;
  5809	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    another is to bring out the antithesis between 'head' and 'hand.'
  5810	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5811	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] 'Þæt þæt fýr' (2702), S. emends to 'þá þæt fýr' = _when the fire
  5812	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    began to grow less intense afterward_. This emendation relieves the
  5813	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    passage of a plethora of conjunctive _þæt_'s.
  5814	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5815	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] For 'gefyldan' (2707), S. proposes 'gefylde.' The passage would
  5816	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    read: _He felled the foe (life drove out strength), and they then both
  5817	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    had destroyed him, chieftains related_. This gives Beowulf the credit
  5818	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    of having felled the dragon; then they combine to annihilate him.--For
  5819	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'ellen' (2707), Kl. suggests 'e(a)llne.'--The reading '_life drove out
  5820	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    strength_' is very unsatisfactory and very peculiar. I would suggest
  5821	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    as follows: Adopt S.'s emendation, remove H.'s parenthesis, read
  5822	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'ferh-ellen wræc,' and translate: _He felled the foe, drove out his
  5823	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    life-strength_ (that is, made him _hors de combat_), _and then they
  5824	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    both, etc_.

  5833	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5834	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf fulfils his lord's behest.}

  5836	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then heard I that Wihstan's son very quickly,
  5837	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          These words being uttered, heeded his liegelord
  5838	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wounded and war-sick, went in his armor,
  5839	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His well-woven ring-mail, 'neath the roof of the barrow.
  5840	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Then the trusty retainer treasure-gems many
  5841	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5842	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dragon's den.}
  5843	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5844	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Victorious saw, when the seat he came near to,
  5845	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gold-treasure sparkling spread on the bottom,
  5846	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wonder on the wall, and the worm-creature's cavern,
  5847	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ancient dawn-flier's, vessels a-standing,
  5848	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Cups of the ancients of cleansers bereavèd,
  5849	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Robbed of their ornaments: there were helmets in numbers,
  5850	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Old and rust-eaten, arm-bracelets many,
  5851	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Artfully woven. Wealth can easily,
  5852	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gold on the sea-bottom, turn into vanity[1]
  5853	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Each one of earthmen, arm him who pleaseth!
  5854	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And he saw there lying an all-golden banner
  5855	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          High o'er the hoard, of hand-wonders greatest,
  5856	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Linkèd with lacets: a light from it sparkled,
  5857	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That the floor of the cavern he was able to look on,

  5860	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5861	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 To examine the jewels. Sight of the dragon
  5862	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[94]      Not any was offered, but edge offcarried him.
  5863	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5864	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf bears the hoard away.}
  5865	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5866	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then I heard that the hero the hoard-treasure plundered,
  5867	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The giant-work ancient reaved in the cavern,
  5868	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bare on his bosom the beakers and platters,
  5869	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 As himself would fain have it, and took off the standard,
  5870	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The brightest of beacons;[2] the bill had erst injured
  5871	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          (Its edge was of iron), the old-ruler's weapon,
  5872	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Him who long had watched as ward of the jewels,
  5873	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who fire-terror carried hot for the treasure,
  5874	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 Rolling in battle, in middlemost darkness,

  5877	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Curiosity urged him if, excellent-mooded,

  5880	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Mid the jewels he found then the famous old chieftain,
  5881	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His liegelord belovèd, at his life's-end gory:
  5882	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He thereupon 'gan to lave him with water,
  5883	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Till the point of his word piercèd his breast-hoard.
  5884	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Beowulf spake (the gold-gems he noticed),

  5904	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Beowulf's barrow, those who barks ever-dashing

  5906	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  5913	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  5917	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of Wægmunding people: Weird hath offcarried
  5918	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          All of my kinsmen to the Creator's glory,
  5919	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Earls in their vigor: I shall after them fare."
  5920	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Twas the aged liegelord's last-spoken word in
  5921	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 His musings of spirit, ere he mounted the fire,
  5922	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The battle-waves burning: from his bosom departed
  5923	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          His soul to seek the sainted ones' glory.

  5925	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] The word 'oferhígian' (2767) being vague and little understood,
  5926	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    two quite distinct translations of this passage have arisen. One takes
  5927	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'oferhígian' as meaning 'to exceed,' and, inserting 'hord' after
  5928	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'gehwone,' renders: _The treasure may easily, the gold in the ground,
  5929	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    exceed in value every hoard of man, hide it who will._ The other takes
  5930	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'oferhígian' as meaning 'to render arrogant,' and, giving the sentence
  5931	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    a moralizing tone, renders substantially as in the body of this work.
  5932	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    (Cf. 28_13 et seq.)

  5935	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    old lord' is by some regarded as Beowulf's sword; by others, as that
  5936	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    of the ancient possessor of the hoard. 'Ær gescód' (2778), translated
  5937	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    in this work as verb and adverb, is by some regarded as a compound

  5944	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5945	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tTHE DEAD FOES.--WIGLAF'S BITTER TAUNTS.
  5946	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5947	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5948	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf is sorely grieved to see his lord look so un-warlike.}
  5949	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5950	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          It had wofully chanced then the youthful retainer
  5951	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To behold on earth the most ardent-belovèd
  5952	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          At his life-days' limit, lying there helpless.
  5953	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The slayer too lay there, of life all bereavèd,
  5954	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Horrible earth-drake, harassed with sorrow:
  5955	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5956	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The dragon has plundered his last hoard.}
  5957	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5958	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The round-twisted monster was permitted no longer
  5959	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To govern the ring-hoards, but edges of war-swords
  5960	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mightily seized him, battle-sharp, sturdy
  5961	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Leavings of hammers, that still from his wounds
  5962	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 The flier-from-farland fell to the earth
  5963	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hard by his hoard-house, hopped he at midnight
  5964	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not e'er through the air, nor exulting in jewels
  5965	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Suffered them to see him: but he sank then to earthward
  5966	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Through the hero-chief's handwork. I heard sure it throve then
  5967	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5968	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[96]
  5969	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5970	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Few warriors dared to face the monster.}
  5971	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5972	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 But few in the land of liegemen of valor,
  5973	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Though of every achievement bold he had proved him,
  5974	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To run 'gainst the breath of the venomous scather,
  5975	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Or the hall of the treasure to trouble with hand-blows,
  5976	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          If he watching had found the ward of the hoard-hall
  5977	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 On the barrow abiding. Beowulf's part of
  5978	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The treasure of jewels was paid for with death;
  5979	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Each of the twain had attained to the end of
  5980	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Life so unlasting. Not long was the time till
  5981	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5982	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The cowardly thanes come out of the thicket.}
  5983	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5984	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The tardy-at-battle returned from the thicket,
  5985	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 The timid truce-breakers ten all together,
  5986	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who durst not before play with the lances
  5987	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In the prince of the people's pressing emergency;
  5988	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5989	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{They are ashamed of their desertion.}
  5990	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  5991	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But blushing with shame, with shields they betook them,
  5992	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With arms and armor where the old one was lying:
  5993	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 They gazed upon Wiglaf. He was sitting exhausted,
  5994	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Foot-going fighter, not far from the shoulders
  5995	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of the lord of the people, would rouse him with water;
  5996	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          No whit did it help him; though he hoped for it keenly,
  5997	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He was able on earth not at all in the leader
  5998	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Life to retain, and nowise to alter
  5999	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The will of the Wielder; the World-Ruler's power[1]
  6000	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Would govern the actions of each one of heroes,
  6001	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6002	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf is ready to excoriate them.}
  6003	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6004	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As yet He is doing. From the young one forthwith then
  6005	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Could grim-worded greeting be got for him quickly
  6006	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Whose courage had failed him. Wiglaf discoursed then,
  6007	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Weohstan his son, sad-mooded hero,
  6008	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6009	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He begins to taunt them.}
  6010	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6011	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Looked on the hated: "He who soothness will utter
  6012	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Can say that the liegelord who gave you the jewels,
  6013	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ornament-armor wherein ye are standing,
  6014	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 When on ale-bench often he offered to hall-men
  6015	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Helmet and burnie, the prince to his liegemen,
  6016	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As best upon earth he was able to find him,--
  6017	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6018	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[97]
  6019	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6020	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Surely our lord wasted his armor on poltroons.}
  6021	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6022	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That he wildly wasted his war-gear undoubtedly
  6023	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When battle o'ertook him.[2] The troop-king no need had
  6024	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 To glory in comrades; yet God permitted him,
  6025	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6026	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He, however, got along without you}
  6027	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6028	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Victory-Wielder, with weapon unaided
  6029	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Himself to avenge, when vigor was needed.
  6030	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          I life-protection but little was able
  6031	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To give him in battle, and I 'gan, notwithstanding,
  6032	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6033	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{With some aid, I could have saved our liegelord}
  6034	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6035	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 Helping my kinsman (my strength overtaxing):
  6036	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He waxed the weaker when with weapon I smote on
  6037	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          My mortal opponent, the fire less strongly
  6038	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Flamed from his bosom. Too few of protectors
  6039	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Came round the king at the critical moment.
  6040	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6041	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Gift-giving is over with your people: the ring-lord is dead.}
  6042	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6043	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Now must ornament-taking and weapon-bestowing,
  6044	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Home-joyance all, cease for your kindred,
  6045	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Food for the people; each of your warriors
  6046	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Must needs be bereavèd of rights that he holdeth
  6047	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In landed possessions, when faraway nobles
  6048	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Shall learn of your leaving your lord so basely,
  6049	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6050	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{What is life without honor?}
  6051	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6052	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The dastardly deed. Death is more pleasant
  6053	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To every earlman than infamous life is!"
  6054	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  6056	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    _The might (or judgment) of God would determine death for every man,

  6074	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then he charged that the battle be announced at the hedge

  6089	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          By the deeds of the dragon in death-bed abideth;

  6098	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Earl o'er another whose end-day hath reached him,
  6099	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Head-watch holdeth o'er heroes unliving,[1]
  6100	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6101	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Our lord's death will lead to attacks from our old foes.}
  6102	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6103	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          For friend and for foeman. The folk now expecteth
  6104	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 A season of strife when the death of the folk-king
  6105	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To Frankmen and Frisians in far-lands is published.
  6106	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The war-hatred waxed warm 'gainst the Hugmen,
  6107	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  6110	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When Higelac came with an army of vessels
  6111	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Faring to Friesland, where the Frankmen in battle
  6112	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Humbled him and bravely with overmight 'complished

  6115	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The atheling to earlmen; aye was denied us
  6116	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Merewing's mercy. The men of the Swedelands
  6117	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 For truce or for truth trust I but little;
  6118	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But widely 'twas known that near Ravenswood Ongentheow

  6159	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The death-rush of warmen, widely was noticed,
  6160	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          How the folks with each other feud did awaken.
  6161	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The worthy one went then[1] with well-beloved comrades,
  6162	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Old and dejected to go to the fastness,
  6163	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ongentheo earl upward then turned him;
  6164	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of Higelac's battle he'd heard on inquiry,
  6165	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The exultant one's prowess, despaired of resistance,
  6166	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          With earls of the ocean to be able to struggle,
  6167	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 'Gainst sea-going sailors to save the hoard-treasure,

  6169	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Old 'neath the earth-wall. Then was offered pursuance
  6170	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To the braves of the Swedemen, the banner[2] to Higelac.
  6171	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[100]     They fared then forth o'er the field-of-protection,

  6184	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  6188	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 When the king of the thane-troop thither did turn him:
  6189	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The wise-mooded son of Wonred was powerless

  6205	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Shepherd of people, was pierced to the vitals.

  6207	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Carried him quickly when occasion was granted
  6208	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That the place of the slain they were suffered to manage.

  6236	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 That's the feud and hatred--as ween I 'twill happen--

  6242	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The deed-mighty Scyldings,[4] did for the troopers
  6243	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          What best did avail them, and further moreover
  6244	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6245	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{It is time for us to pay the last marks of respect to our lord.}
  6246	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6247	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hero-deeds 'complished. Now is haste most fitting,
  6248	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That the lord of liegemen we look upon yonder,
  6249	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 And _that_ one carry on journey to death-pyre
  6250	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who ring-presents gave us. Not aught of it all
  6251	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Shall melt with the brave one--there's a mass of bright jewels,

  6253	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And ending it all ornament-rings too
  6254	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 Bought with his life; these fire shall devour,
  6255	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Flame shall cover, no earlman shall wear
  6256	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A jewel-memento, nor beautiful virgin
  6257	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Have on her neck rings to adorn her,
  6258	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          But wretched in spirit bereavèd of gold-gems
  6259	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 She shall oft with others be exiled and banished,
  6260	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Since the leader of liegemen hath laughter forsaken,
  6261	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[102]     Mirth and merriment. Hence many a war-spear
  6262	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Cold from the morning shall be clutched in the fingers,
  6263	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Heaved in the hand, no harp-music's sound shall
  6264	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       80 Waken the warriors, but the wan-coated raven
  6265	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fain over fey ones freely shall gabble,
  6266	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Shall say to the eagle how he sped in the eating,
  6267	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When, the wolf his companion, he plundered the slain."
  6268	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So the high-minded hero was rehearsing these stories
  6269	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       85 Loathsome to hear; he lied as to few of
  6270	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6271	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The warriors go sadly to look at Beowulf's lifeless body.}
  6272	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6273	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Weirds and of words. All the war-troop arose then,
  6274	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Neath the Eagle's Cape sadly betook them,
  6275	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Weeping and woful, the wonder to look at.
  6276	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They saw on the sand then soulless a-lying,
  6277	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       90 His slaughter-bed holding, him who rings had given them
  6278	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          In days that were done; then the death-bringing moment
  6279	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was come to the good one, that the king very warlike,
  6280	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wielder of Weders, with wonder-death perished.
  6281	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          First they beheld there a creature more wondrous,
  6282	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6283	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{They also see the dragon.}
  6284	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6285	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       95 The worm on the field, in front of them lying,
  6286	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The foeman before them: the fire-spewing dragon,
  6287	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Ghostly and grisly guest in his terrors,
  6288	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Was scorched in the fire; as he lay there he measured
  6289	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fifty of feet; came forth in the night-time[5]
  6290	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t      100 To rejoice in the air, thereafter departing
  6291	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To visit his den; he in death was then fastened,
  6292	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He would joy in no other earth-hollowed caverns.
  6293	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          There stood round about him beakers and vessels,
  6294	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Dishes were lying and dear-valued weapons,
  6295	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t      105 With iron-rust eaten, as in earth's mighty bosom
  6296	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A thousand of winters there they had rested:
  6297	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6298	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{The hoard was under a magic spell.}
  6299	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6300	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That mighty bequest then with magic was guarded,
  6301	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gold of the ancients, that earlman not any
  6302	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The ring-hall could touch, save Ruling-God only,
  6303	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[103] 110 Sooth-king of Vict'ries gave whom He wished to
  6304	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6305	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{God alone could give access to it.}
  6306	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6307	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          [6](He is earth-folk's protector) to open the treasure,
  6308	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          E'en to such among mortals as seemed to Him proper.
  6309	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6310	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] For 'góda,' which seems a surprising epithet for a Geat to apply
  6311	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    to the "terrible" Ongentheow, B. suggests 'gomela.' The passage would
  6312	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    then stand: '_The old one went then,' etc._
  6313	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6314	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] For 'segn Higeláce,' K., Th., and B. propose 'segn Higeláces,'
  6315	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    meaning: _Higelac's banner followed the Swedes (in pursuit)._--S.
  6316	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    suggests 'sæcc Higeláces,' and renders: _Higelac's pursuit._--The
  6317	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    H.-So. reading, as translated in our text, means that the banner of
  6318	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    the enemy was captured and brought to Higelac as a trophy.
  6319	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6320	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [3] The rendering given in this translation represents the king as
  6321	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    being generous beyond the possibility of reproach; but some
  6322	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    authorities construe 'him' (2996) as plu., and understand the passage
  6323	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    to mean that no one reproached the two brothers with having received
  6324	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    more reward than they were entitled to.
  6325	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6326	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [4] The name 'Scyldingas' here (3006) has caused much discussion, and
  6327	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    given rise to several theories, the most important of which are as
  6328	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    follows: (1) After the downfall of Hrothgar's family, Beowulf was king
  6329	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    of the Danes, or Scyldings. (2) For 'Scyldingas' read
  6330	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'Scylfingas'--that is, after killing Eadgils, the Scylfing prince,
  6331	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    Beowulf conquered his land, and held it in subjection. (3) M.
  6332	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    considers 3006 a thoughtless repetition of 2053. (Cf. H.-So.)
  6333	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6334	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [5] B. takes 'nihtes' and 'hwílum' (3045) as separate adverbial cases,
  6335	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    and renders: _Joy in the air had he of yore by night, etc_. He thinks
  6336	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    that the idea of vanished time ought to be expressed.
  6337	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6338	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [6] The parenthesis is by some emended so as to read: (1) (_He_ (i.e.
  6339	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    _God_) _is the hope of men_); (2) (_he is the hope of heroes_). Gr.'s
  6340	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    reading has no parenthesis, but says: ... _could touch, unless God
  6341	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    himself, true king of victories, gave to whom he would to open the
  6342	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    treasure, the secret place of enchanters, etc_. The last is rejected
  6343	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    on many grounds.

  6350	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tWIGLAF'S SAD STORY.--THE HOARD CARRIED OFF.
  6351	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6352	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6353	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then 'twas seen that the journey prospered him little
  6354	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who wrongly within had the ornaments hidden[1]
  6355	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Down 'neath the wall. The warden erst slaughtered
  6356	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Some few of the folk-troop: the feud then thereafter
  6357	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t        5 Was hotly avengèd. 'Tis a wonder where,[2]
  6358	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When the strength-famous trooper has attained to the end of
  6359	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Life-days allotted, then no longer the man may
  6360	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Remain with his kinsmen where mead-cups are flowing.
  6361	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So to Beowulf happened when the ward of the barrow,
  6362	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Assaults, he sought for: himself had no knowledge
  6363	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          How his leaving this life was likely to happen.
  6364	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So to doomsday, famous folk-leaders down did
  6365	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Call it with curses--who 'complished it there--
  6366	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[104]     That that man should be ever of ill-deeds convicted,
  6367	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       15 Confined in foul-places, fastened in hell-bonds,
  6368	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Punished with plagues, who this place should e'er ravage.[3]
  6369	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          He cared not for gold: rather the Wielder's
  6370	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Favor preferred he first to get sight of.[4]
  6371	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6372	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf addresses his comrades.}
  6373	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6374	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Wiglaf discoursed then, Wihstan his son:
  6375	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       20 "Oft many an earlman on one man's account must
  6376	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Sorrow endure, as to us it hath happened.
  6377	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The liegelord belovèd we could little prevail on,
  6378	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Kingdom's keeper, counsel to follow,
  6379	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not to go to the guardian of the gold-hoard, but let him
  6380	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 Lie where he long was, live in his dwelling
  6381	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Till the end of the world. Met we a destiny
  6382	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Hard to endure: the hoard has been looked at,
  6383	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Been gained very grimly; too grievous the fate that[5]
  6384	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The prince of the people pricked to come thither.
  6385	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 _I_ was therein and all of it looked at,
  6386	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The building's equipments, since access was given me,
  6387	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Not kindly at all entrance permitted
  6388	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6389	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{He tells them of Beowulf's last moments.}
  6390	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6391	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Within under earth-wall. Hastily seized I
  6392	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And held in my hands a huge-weighing burden
  6393	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       35 Of hoard-treasures costly, hither out bare them
  6394	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          To my liegelord belovèd: life was yet in him,
  6395	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And consciousness also; the old one discoursed then
  6396	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Much and mournfully, commanded to greet you,
  6397	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6398	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Beowulf's dying request.}
  6399	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6400	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bade that remembering the deeds of your friend-lord
  6401	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 Ye build on the fire-hill of corpses a lofty
  6402	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Burial-barrow, broad and far-famous,
  6403	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As 'mid world-dwelling warriors he was widely most honored
  6404	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          While he reveled in riches. Let us rouse us and hasten
  6405	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[105]     Again to see and seek for the treasure,
  6406	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 The wonder 'neath wall. The way I will show you,
  6407	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          That close ye may look at ring-gems sufficient
  6408	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And gold in abundance. Let the bier with promptness
  6409	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fully be fashioned, when forth we shall come,
  6410	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And lift we our lord, then, where long he shall tarry,
  6411	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       50 Well-beloved warrior, 'neath the Wielder's protection."
  6412	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6413	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Wiglaf charges them to build a funeral-pyre.}
  6414	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6415	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Then the son of Wihstan bade orders be given,
  6416	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mood-valiant man, to many of heroes,
  6417	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Holders of homesteads, that they hither from far,
  6418	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          [6]Leaders of liegemen, should look for the good one
  6419	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       55 With wood for his pyre: "The flame shall now swallow
  6420	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          (The wan fire shall wax[7]) the warriors' leader
  6421	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who the rain of the iron often abided,
  6422	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          When, sturdily hurled, the storm of the arrows
  6423	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Leapt o'er linden-wall, the lance rendered service,
  6424	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       60 Furnished with feathers followed the arrow."
  6425	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Now the wise-mooded son of Wihstan did summon
  6426	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The best of the braves from the band of the ruler
  6427	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  6430	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Seven together; 'neath the enemy's roof he
  6431	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Went with the seven; one of the heroes
  6432	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       65 Who fared at the front, a fire-blazing torch-light
  6433	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bare in his hand. No lot then decided
  6434	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Who that hoard should havoc, when hero-earls saw it

  6436	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Rusting to ruin: they rued then but little
  6437	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       70 That they hastily hence hauled out the treasure,

  6443	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[106]     The waters enwind the ward of the treasures.

  6448	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       75 A mass unmeasured, the men-leader off then,
  6449	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The hero hoary, to Whale's-Ness was carried.

  6451	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [1] For 'gehýdde,' B. suggests 'gehýðde': the passage would stand as
  6452	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    above except the change of 'hidden' (v. 2) to 'plundered.' The
  6453	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    reference, however, would be to the thief, not to the dragon.
  6454	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6455	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [2] The passage 'Wundur ... búan' (3063-3066), M. took to be a
  6456	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    question asking whether it was strange that a man should die when his
  6457	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    appointed time had come.--B. sees a corruption, and makes emendations
  6458	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    introducing the idea that a brave man should not die from sickness or
  6459	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    from old age, but should find death in the performance of some deed of
  6460	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    daring.--S. sees an indirect question introduced by 'hwár' and
  6461	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    dependent upon 'wundur': _A secret is it when the hero is to die,
  6462	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    etc_.--Why may the two clauses not be parallel, and the whole passage
  6463	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    an Old English cry of '_How wonderful is death!'?_--S.'s is the best
  6464	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    yet offered, if 'wundor' means 'mystery.'
  6465	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  6467	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    'ravage' (v. 16) to be changed to 'tread.'
  6468	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6469	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [4] 'He cared ... sight of' (17, 18), S. emends so as to read as

  6475	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6476	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [6] 'Folc-ágende' (3114) B. takes as dat. sing. with 'gódum,' and

  6478	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    where the good folk-ruler lay_.

  6480	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t    [7] C. proposes to take 'weaxan' = L. 'vescor,' and translate

  6496	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A pile on the earth strong for the burning,
  6497	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Behung with helmets, hero-knights' targets,
  6498	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And bright-shining burnies, as he begged they should have them;

  6500	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Their liegelord beloved, laid in the middle.

  6505	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The largest of dead-fires: dark o'er the vapor
  6506	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The smoke-cloud ascended, the sad-roaring fire,
  6507	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       10 Mingled with weeping (the wind-roar subsided)

  6511	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And mournful measures the much-grieving widow

  6520	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6521	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The men of the Weders made accordingly
  6522	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          A hill on the height, high and extensive,
  6523	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Of sea-going sailors to be seen from a distance,
  6524	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          And the brave one's beacon built where the fire was,
  6525	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       25 In ten-days' space, with a wall surrounded it,
  6526	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As wisest of world-folk could most worthily plan it.
  6527	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          They placed in the barrow rings and jewels,

  6529	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[107]
  6530	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6531	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{Rings and gems are laid in the barrow.}
  6532	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6533	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          All such ornaments as erst in the treasure
  6534	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          War-mooded men had won in possession:
  6535	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       30 The earnings of earlmen to earth they entrusted,
  6536	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          The gold to the dust, where yet it remaineth
  6537	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          As useless to mortals as in foregoing eras.
  6538	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          'Round the dead-mound rode then the doughty-in-battle,
  6539	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Bairns of all twelve of the chiefs of the people,
  6540	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6541	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{They mourn for their lord, and sing his praises.}
  6542	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t

  6544	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Speak in measure, mention him with pleasure,
  6545	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Weighed his worth, and his warlike achievements
  6546	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Mightily commended, as 'tis meet one praise his
  6547	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Liegelord in words and love him in spirit,
  6548	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       40 When forth from his body he fares to destruction.
  6549	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          So lamented mourning the men of the Geats,
  6550	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Fond-loving vassals, the fall of their lord,
  6551	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6552	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t{An ideal king.}
  6553	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6554	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Said he was kindest of kings under heaven,
  6555	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t          Gentlest of men, most winning of manner,
  6556	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t       45 Friendliest to folk-troops and fondest of honor.

  6563	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tADDENDA.
  6564	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6565	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6566	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tSeveral discrepancies and other oversights have been noticed in the H.-So.
  6567	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tglossary. Of these a good part were avoided by Harrison and Sharp, the
  6568	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tAmerican editors of Beowulf, in their last edition, 1888. The rest will, I
  6569	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\thope, be noticed in their fourth edition. As, however, this book may fall
  6570	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tinto the hands of some who have no copy of the American edition, it seems
  6571	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tbest to notice all the principal oversights of the German editors.
  6572	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6573	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~From hám~ (194).--Notes and glossary conflict; the latter not having been
  6574	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\taltered to suit the conclusions accepted in the former.
  6575	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6576	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~Þær gelýfan sceal dryhtnes dóme~ (440).--Under 'dóm' H. says 'the might
  6577	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tof the Lord'; while under 'gelýfan' he says 'the judgment of the Lord.'
  6578	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6579	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~Eal bencþelu~ (486).--Under 'benc-þelu' H. says _nom. plu._; while under
  6580	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t'eal' he says _nom. sing._
  6581	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6582	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~Heatho-ræmas~ (519).--Under 'ætberan' H. translates 'to the Heathoremes';
  6583	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\twhile under 'Heatho-ræmas' he says 'Heathoræmas reaches Breca in the
  6584	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tswimming-match with Beowulf.' Harrison and Sharp (3d edition, 1888) avoid
  6585	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tthe discrepancy.
  6586	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6587	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~Fáh féond-scaða~ (554).--Under 'féond-scaða' H. says 'a gleaming
  6588	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tsea-monster'; under 'fáh' he says 'hostile.'
  6589	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6590	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~Onfeng hraðe inwit-þancum~ (749).--Under 'onfón' H. says 'he _received_
  6591	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tthe maliciously-disposed one'; under 'inwit-þanc' he says 'he _grasped_,'
  6592	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tetc.
  6593	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6594	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~Níð-wundor séon~ (1366).--Under 'níð-wundor' H. calls this word itself
  6595	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t_nom. sing._; under 'séon' he translates it as accus. sing., understanding
  6596	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t'man' as subject of 'séon.' H. and S. (3d edition) make the correction.
  6597	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6598	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~Forgeaf hilde-bille~ (1521).--H., under the second word, calls it instr.
  6599	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tdat.; while under 'forgifan' he makes it the dat. of indir. obj. H. and S.
  6600	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t(3d edition) make the change.
  6601	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6602	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~Brád~ and ~brún-ecg~ (1547).--Under 'brád' H. says 'das breite Hüftmesser
  6603	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tmit bronzener Klinge'; under 'brún-ecg' he says 'ihr breites Hüftmesser
  6604	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tmit blitzender Klinge.'
  6605	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6606	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t[110]
  6607	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6608	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~Yðelíce~ (1557).--Under this word H. makes it modify 'ástód.' If this be
  6609	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tright, the punctuation of the fifth edition is wrong. See H. and S.,
  6610	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tappendix.
  6611	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6612	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~Sélran gesóhte~ (1840).--Under 'sél' and 'gesécan' H. calls these two
  6613	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\twords accus. plu.; but this is clearly an error, as both are nom. plu.,
  6614	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tpred. nom. H. and S. correct under 'sél.'
  6615	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6616	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~Wið sylfne~ (1978).--Under 'wið' and 'gesittan' H. says 'wið = near, by';
  6617	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tunder 'self' he says 'opposite.'
  6618	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6619	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~þéow~ (2225) is omitted from the glossary.
  6620	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6621	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~For duguðum~ (2502).--Under 'duguð' H. translates this phrase, 'in
  6622	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tTüchtigkeit'; under 'for,' by 'vor der edlen Kriegerschaar.'
  6623	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6624	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~þær~ (2574).--Under 'wealdan' H. translates _þær_ by 'wo'; under 'mótan,'
  6625	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tby 'da.' H. and S. suggest 'if' in both passages.
  6626	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6627	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~Wunde~ (2726).--Under 'wund' H. says 'dative,' and under 'wæl-bléate' he
  6628	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tsays 'accus.' It is without doubt accus., parallel with 'benne.'
  6629	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6630	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~Strengum gebæded~ (3118).--Under 'strengo' H. says 'Strengum' = mit
  6631	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tMacht; under 'gebæded' he translates 'von den Sehnen.' H. and S. correct
  6632	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tthis discrepancy by rejecting the second reading.
  6633	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6634	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t~Bronda be láfe~ (3162).--A recent emendation. The fourth edition had
  6635	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t'bronda betost.' In the fifth edition the editor neglects to change the
  6636	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\tglossary to suit the new emendation. See 'bewyrcan.'
  6637	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6638	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6639	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6640	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
  6641	BeowulfbyJLesslieHall.txt\t
